\section{Explicit Hessian-Projector Extraction for the Remaining Graded \(2+2\) Coefficient Point}

\section{Goal}

The only remaining microscopic coefficient problem is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O,
}
\]
with possible subleading corrections from \(OD,DO,DD\).

In the exact concrete Class II-compatible branch,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so the longitudinal channel must be read from the Branch-B primitive coefficient
\[
\lambda_c.
\]

\section{1. Full first-order transport extraction}

Write the background-dependent Hessian in block form
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal H_{TT} & \mathcal H_{TO} & \mathcal H_{TD}\\
\mathcal H_{OT} & \mathcal H_{OO} & \mathcal H_{OD}\\
\mathcal H_{DT} & \mathcal H_{DO} & \mathcal H_{DD}
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and expand each block as
\[
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H_{AB}^{(0)}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\mathcal W_{AB}^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
\]
Only \(\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}\) contributes to the principal graded transport symbol.

After restriction to the tangent bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}Q_B=2,
\]
define the \(Q_B\)-endomorphism-valued first-order block kernel
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
\]

\section{2. Canonical projector functionals}

Let \(\Sigma_a\) denote the Pauli basis on \(Q_B\), and let
\[
(\hat n,e_1,e_2)
\]
be the shell-adapted orthonormal frame.

Define the three invariant projectors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu\bigr),
}
\label{eq:Ppar_def_new}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\operatorname{Tr}_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
}
\label{eq:PE_def_new}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\operatorname{Tr}_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\label{eq:PO_def_new}
\end{equation}

These extract, respectively, the longitudinal singlet, the even transverse doublet,
and the odd transverse doublet.

\section{3. \(OO\)-block longitudinal extraction}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{OO}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:VOO_new}
\end{equation}
Its longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:a3OO_new}
\end{equation}

Because of the oddness filter, its principal branch-sensitive expansion has the form
\begin{equation}
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\,\theta'(\xi)
+
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^3
+
O\!\bigl(\theta'(\xi)\theta(\xi)^2,\theta'(\xi)^5\bigr).
\label{eq:a3OO_expansion_new}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact coefficient identification is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\parallel;OO}^{(0)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},
\qquad
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:OO_identification_new}
\end{equation}

In the current concrete Class II-compatible branch,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so the practical longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=\lambda_{c;OO}=2\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_c_from_OO_new}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, one may write the executable limit formula
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
2\lim_{\theta'\to 0}
\frac{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_c_limit_new}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Why the primitive longitudinal seed starts at \(\theta'^3\)}

The microscopic longitudinal primitive channel is generated by
\[
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\]
Its direct \(Q_B\)-restriction vanishes,
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\]
but its square is nontrivial:
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\Sigma_3\bigr).
\]
Taking the traceless part gives
\[
S_\xi
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\Sigma_3.
\]
Since the overlap \(f_+f_-\theta'(\xi)^2\) is parity-even and integrates to zero in the graded channel,
one needs one additional odd factor.
Hence the good longitudinal transport channel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Vpar_prim_new}
\end{equation}
This is the Branch-B primitive longitudinal seed.

\section{5. \(TD+DT\)-block transverse extraction}

Define the mixed transverse carrier
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
:=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:MTDDT_new}
\end{equation}

Its leading even/odd transverse coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}].
}
\label{eq:e0o0_TDDT_new}
\end{equation}

In the minimal mixed-block truncation, these are identified with the actual transverse coefficient point:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_0^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:LambdaEO_from_TDDT_new}
\end{equation}

More broadly, beyond the minimal truncation one has
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_E
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\label{eq:LambdaEO_sum_new}
\end{equation}
but the sharp current leading-order audit starts from \(TD+DT\).

\section{6. Reduced PDE coefficients}

Once \(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\) are extracted, the reduced coefficients follow from
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:reduced_dictionary_new}
\end{equation}

Using
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:lambda_final_new}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_final_new}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Current working-branch Schur-complement realization}

For the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch,
integrating out the heavy mediator \(X_i^a\) gives the Schur correction
\begin{equation}
\Delta_X^{(2)}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\delta J+\beta_X\delta K\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\delta J+\beta_X\delta K\bigr)^\dagger.
\label{eq:DX2_new}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\Delta_X^{(2)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\delta J\delta J^\dagger
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger\bigr)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\delta K\delta K^\dagger.
\label{eq:DX2_split_new}
\end{equation}

The sharp working-branch identification is then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(JJ\)-piece feeds the primitive longitudinal slot;
\item the mixed \(JK+KJ\)-piece feeds the transverse \(E/O\) slots;
\item the pure \(K\)-sector is transverse at principal order and does not generate \(\lambda_c\).
\end{enumerate}

Accordingly, the branch-level coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
c_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
c_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:working_branch_cpoint_new}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
\alpha
=
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:working_branch_witness_new}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest closure statement}

What is fully closed now is the extraction \emph{protocol}:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]
What is also closed on the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch is the Schur-reduced coefficient pattern
\eqref{eq:working_branch_cpoint_new}--\eqref{eq:working_branch_witness_new}.

What is still not yet unconditional is the final source-by-source differentiation of the
\emph{complete} microscopic TECT Hessian yielding the exact numerical functions
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\qquad h_{11}(\theta),\qquad h_{12}(\theta),\qquad h_{21}(\theta),\qquad h_{22}(\theta).
\]
So the genuine remaining frontier is not structural.
It is the explicit insertion of the full complete TECT background into
\[
\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}(\xi)+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}(\xi).
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The graded \(2+2\) bypass route is already structurally closed.

In the exact concrete Class II-compatible branch,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so the remaining coefficient point is
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

The exact blockwise extraction protocol is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}
\to
V^\mu_{OO}
\to
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3 n_\mu V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\bigr)
\to
\lambda_c,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}
\to
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
\to
e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)}
\to
\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

After overlap insertion,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\]
hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Therefore the remaining frontier is not conceptual.
It is the literal differentiation and projection of the complete background-dependent Hessian blocks
\[
\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}(\xi)+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}(\xi).
\]

\section{Executable Hessian Extraction of the Remaining Graded \(2+2\) Coefficient Point}

\section{Goal}

The remaining microscopic problem is not conceptual anymore.
It is the explicit extraction of
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O
}
\]
from the background-dependent first-order Hessian transport kernel.

At the current sharpest blockwise stage, this reduces to
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

\section{Universal first-order Hessian template}

Let the full fluctuation field be decomposed as
\[
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta),
\qquad
a\sim T,\quad \nu\sim O,\quad \zeta\sim D.
\]
Around the shell-/defect-adapted background \(\bar\Phi_{\min}\), the full Hessian has block form
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal H_{TT} & \mathcal H_{TO} & \mathcal H_{TD}\\
\mathcal H_{OT} & \mathcal H_{OO} & \mathcal H_{OD}\\
\mathcal H_{DT} & \mathcal H_{DO} & \mathcal H_{DD}
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with blockwise expansion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H_{AB}^{(0)}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\mathcal W_{AB}^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
}
\label{eq:HAB_expand_exec}
\end{equation}
Only the one-derivative kernel \(\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}\) contributes to the principal graded symbol.

Project to the tangent bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}Q_B=2,
\]
and define the projected block kernels
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:MAB_def_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{Canonical projector functionals}

Let \(\Sigma_a\) (\(a=1,2,3\)) denote the Pauli basis on \(Q_B\), and let
\[
(\hat n,E^\mu{}_a,J^\mu{}_a)
\]
be the shell-adapted worldvolume frame.

Define the three invariant coefficient projectors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\mathcal M^\mu\bigr),
}
\label{eq:Ppar_exec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
}
\label{eq:PE_exec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_a\,\mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
}
\label{eq:PO_exec}
\end{equation}

These extract, respectively,
\[
n^\mu\Sigma_3,
\qquad
E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a,
\qquad
J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
\]

\section{OO block: exact longitudinal extraction}

Define the \(OO\)-projected first-order transport block
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{OO}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:VOO_exec}
\end{equation}
Its longitudinal scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:a3OO_exec}
\end{equation}

The branch-sensitive expansion is
\begin{equation}
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\,\theta'(\xi)
+
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^3
+
O(\theta'(\xi)^5,\theta'(\xi)\theta(\xi)^2).
\label{eq:a3OO_branch_expand_exec}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{\parallel;OO}^{(0)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},
\qquad
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:OO_ident_exec}
\end{equation}

In the current concrete Class II-compatible branch,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so the practical longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c=\lambda_{c;OO}=2\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:lambdac_from_OO_exec}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the executable extraction rule is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}
\frac{
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
}.
}
\label{eq:lambdaOO_extract_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{Source-by-source decomposition inside the \(OO\) audit}

At principal order, decompose the local transport kernel as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
V^\mu_{\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
+
V^\mu_K(\xi)
+
V^\mu_{EO}(\xi)
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:V_decomp_exec}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Primitive longitudinal source}

The primitive commutator-square channel is
\[
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]
For the explicit defect representative,
\[
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3.
\]
Hence the primitive transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Vprim_exec}
\end{equation}
Applying the projectors,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{\mathrm{prim}}]
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_E[V_{\mathrm{prim}}]=0,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[V_{\mathrm{prim}}]=0.
}
\label{eq:Pprim_exec}
\end{equation}

\subsection{K-sector source}

The \(K\)-sector tangent block has the universal form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_K^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\kappa_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\kappa_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:VK_exec}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_K]=0,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_E[V_K]=\kappa_E(\xi)\theta'(\xi),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[V_K]=\kappa_O(\xi)\theta'(\xi).
}
\label{eq:PK_exec}
\end{equation}

\subsection{EO-slot source}

The explicit \(E/O\)-slot contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:VEO_exec}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{EO}]=0,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_E[V_{EO}]
=
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[V_{EO}]
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:PEO_exec}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Immediate principal-order consequence}

Hence the principal source table is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{source}
&
\mathfrak P_\parallel
&
\mathfrak P_E
&
\mathfrak P_O
\\\hline
V_{\mathrm{prim}}
&
\dfrac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^3
&
0
&
0
\\
V_K
&
0
&
\kappa_E\theta'
&
\kappa_O\theta'
\\
V_{EO}
&
0
&
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'\cos\theta
&
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'\cos\theta
\\
V_{\mathrm{irr}}
&
0\ \text{(at principal order)}
&
0\ \text{(at principal order)}
&
0\ \text{(at principal order)}
\end{array}
}
\label{eq:source_table_exec}
\end{equation}

Therefore the principal longitudinal source is unique:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
a_3^{(EO)}=0,
\qquad
a_3^{(\mathrm{prim})}=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:a3_unique_exec}
\end{equation}

This proves that, at the current solved leading stage, the \(OO\) longitudinal audit is exactly the extraction of the \(\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\Sigma_3\) coefficient.

\section{TD+DT block: exact transverse extraction}

Define the mixed transverse carrier
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
:=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:MTDDT_exec}
\end{equation}
Its leading even/odd coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}
=
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}
=
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\mathrm{inv}}].
}
\label{eq:e0o0_exec}
\end{equation}

In the minimal mixed-block truncation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O=o_0^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:LambdaEO_exec}
\end{equation}

Thus the leading transverse kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{corr}},
}
\label{eq:MTDDT_form_exec}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{corr}}\) starts at higher order and/or receives contributions from
\[
OD,\quad DO,\quad DD.
\]

\section{Honest caveat on the transverse sector}

At the reduced branch level, \(TD+DT\) is the correct leading transverse summary.
However, a naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear satisfies
\[
\Sigma_3(\Lambda_E\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O\Sigma_2)
+
(\Lambda_E\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
=
0,
\]
because
\[
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}=\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
\]
Therefore the statement
\[
JK\text{ alone automatically gives the transverse pair}
\]
is too strong.
A genuinely nonzero full-PDE transverse realization requires derivative-resolved and/or phase-resolved microscopic structure.

Thus the current statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
TD+DT\to(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
}
\label{eq:TDDT_honest_exec}
\end{equation}
is a correct branch-level reduced summary,
but not yet the unconditional final microscopic closure of the complete TECT PDE.

\section{Projection to the low modes and reduced PDE coefficients}

Let the even/odd low modes be
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\]
Then the projected mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
}
\label{eq:Mmu_exec}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:coeff_dict_exec}
\end{equation}
Inside the exact concrete Class II branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:coeff_dict_branchB_exec}
\end{equation}

Using the already-evaluated overlap integrals
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
the reduced PDE coefficients become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:lpar_final_exec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:ab_final_exec}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact honest closure statement}

What is now fully closed is the executable extraction protocol:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

What is also closed at principal order is the source table:
only the primitive commutator-square channel contributes to the longitudinal \(n^\mu\Sigma_3\) slot,
while the \(K\)-sector and \(EO\)-slot are purely transverse at this order.

What remains honestly open is the final source-by-source differentiation of the complete microscopic TECT Hessian yielding the explicit functions
\[
\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}(\xi)+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}(\xi),
\]
together with the derivative-resolved transverse realization beyond the naive local \(JK\) truncation.

\section{Final Summary}

In the exact concrete Class II-compatible branch, the longitudinal channel is Branch B:
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
\]
Therefore the remaining coefficient point is
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

The exact executable extraction is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}
\to
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\bigr)
\to
\lambda_{c;OO}\equiv\lambda_c,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}
\to
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
\to
e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)}
\to
\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

At principal order, the source table is:
\[
\boxed{
a_3^{(\mathrm{prim})}=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
a_3^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
a_3^{(EO)}=0,
}
\]
so the longitudinal source is uniquely the primitive commutator-square channel,
while the transverse sector is carried by the mixed transverse blocks.

After overlap insertion,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
}
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

Therefore the genuine remaining frontier is not structural.
It is the literal differentiation and projection of the complete microscopic Hessian blocks
\[
\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}(\xi)+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}(\xi).
\]

\section{Explicit Working-Branch Extraction of \texorpdfstring{$\mathsf N_{ij}^a$}{Nij^a} and \texorpdfstring{$(g_c,g_E,g_O)$}{(gc,gE,gO)} from the Class II TECT Sector}

\section{Short explanation}

The purpose of this section is not to claim the unconditional full microscopic closure of complete TECT.
Rather, the goal is to isolate the strongest currently explicit \emph{working microscopic branch}
in which the transport coefficient point can be written algebraically and matched to the reduced graded \(2+2\) PDE data.

The exact current mainline remains the graded \(2+2\) Hessian extraction problem
\[
OO\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
TD+DT\to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\]
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O
\]
in the present concrete Branch-B realization.

Thus the present section should be read as an explicit Class II \emph{working-branch realization}
of that coefficient point, not as the final unconditional microscopic completion of complete TECT.

\section{1. Class II working microscopic branch}

Introduce a heavy internal vector mediator \(X_i^a\) coupled to the refined locked TECT sector:
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:W_Lmic_classII_corr}
\end{equation}

Since \(M_X^2\gg 1\), the mediator can be integrated out algebraically at quadratic order:
\begin{equation}
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(
\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a
\bigr).
\label{eq:W_Xeom_corr}
\end{equation}

Substituting back gives the exact quadratic Schur correction
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X^{(2)}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a\bigr).
}
\label{eq:W_Schur_exact}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X^{(2)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}JJ
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(JK+KJ)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}KK.
}
\label{eq:W_Schur_split}
\end{equation}

Therefore, if one wishes to keep only the mixed current-current piece,
one must say explicitly that one is working in the reduced mixed-channel truncation:
\begin{equation}
\Delta_X^{(2)}\rightsquigarrow
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(JK+KJ).
\label{eq:W_mixed_only}
\end{equation}
Writing only
\[
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}JK
\]
without this caveat is too strong.

\section{2. Working-branch tensor extraction}

Linearizing the Class II working branch around the locked 12-mode BCC background,
one obtains a shell-enriched gradient-linear transport coupling of the form
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\mathsf N_{ij}^a
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\label{eq:W_Lenr_general}
\end{equation}

At the working-branch level, the induced tensor can be parametrized as
\begin{equation}
\delta \mathsf N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a\,\mathcal C_{ij}^{ab},
\label{eq:W_Nij_branch}
\end{equation}
provided one makes explicit that this is a \emph{branch-level reduced tensor identification},
not yet the final complete-TEXT Hessian-derived universal formula.

In the shell-adapted orthonormal frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\), write the irreducible decomposition
\begin{align}
\mathsf N_{ij}^3 &= g_c\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:W_N3_corr}
\\
\mathsf N_{ij}^1 &= g_E\,\hat n_i e_{1j}-g_O\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:W_N1_corr}
\\
\mathsf N_{ij}^2 &= g_E\,\hat n_i e_{2j}+g_O\,\hat n_i e_{1j}.
\label{eq:W_N2_corr}
\end{align}
Here the notation \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\) is chosen to match directly the graded Branch-B transport point.

\section{3. Relation to the actual graded \(2+2\) mainline}

The true current mainline is not the tensor ansatz by itself.
It is the background-dependent Hessian extraction:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:W_true_mainline}
\end{equation}

Inside the exact concrete Class II-compatible branch,
the present lowest-order solved result is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
}
\label{eq:W_branchB_forced}
\end{equation}
so the longitudinal channel is Branch B, not Branch A.
Accordingly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:W_BranchB_dictionary}
\end{equation}

Therefore the working-branch tensor coefficients must be understood as a branch-level realization of the identifications
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\leftrightarrow \lambda_c,
\qquad
g_E\leftrightarrow \Lambda_E,
\qquad
g_O\leftrightarrow \Lambda_O,
}
\label{eq:W_gc_lambdac_match}
\end{equation}
up to the already-isolated overlap normalization layer.

\section{4. Exact normalization layer}

The overlap-completed reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O.
}
\label{eq:W_exact_norm_layer}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\label{eq:W_g_from_lambdaab}
\end{equation}

Only after explicit overlap evaluation may one specialize to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
C_E=I_\theta^{(E)},
\qquad
C_O=I_\theta^{(O)}.
}
\label{eq:W_Cs_exact}
\end{equation}
If the locked branch symmetry enforces equal transverse overlap,
one may then set
\[
I_\theta^{(E)}=I_\theta^{(O)}=:I_\theta.
\]

Thus the reduced Branch-B coefficients become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha
=
g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta
=
g_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:W_overlap_completed}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Explicit working-branch coefficient point}

At the branch level, the Class II reduction yields the coefficient point
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
c_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
c_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:W_branch_point_c}
\end{equation}
Therefore a natural working-branch identification is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\sim c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\sim c_E,
\qquad
g_O\sim c_O.
}
\label{eq:W_branch_point_g}
\end{equation}

In the canonical normalization where the proportionality constants are absorbed into the overlap layer,
this may be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:W_branch_point_g_canonical}
\end{equation}
However, this must be labeled explicitly as a \emph{working-branch canonical normalization},
not as the unconditional exact coefficient formula of the complete microscopic TECT action.

\section{6. Finite projected extraction pipeline}

The finite extraction protocol may be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
\to
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi]
\to
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
K_i
=
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\big|_{k_*}
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:W_pipeline_corr}
\end{equation}

At the projected level,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3 P_*K_\parallel P_*),
\label{eq:W_trace_lam}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac14
\sum_{a=1}^2
\Tr\!\bigl(
\sigma_a P_*(e_{ai}K_i)P_*
\bigr),
\label{eq:W_trace_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac14
\Bigl[
\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_2P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*\bigr)
-
\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_1P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*\bigr)
\Bigr].
\label{eq:W_trace_beta}
\end{equation}

This is the exact finite projected extraction layer.
What remains open is the literal computation of the projected derivative blocks from the final complete microscopic operator.

\section{7. Honest nondegeneracy statement}

The most accurate nondegeneracy criterion is not an informal determinant statement for an unspecified matrix \(M\),
but the positive-definite symbol condition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:W_G_positive}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:W_g_positive}
\end{equation}

Thus the precise finite working-branch test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:W_finite_test}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest status}

What is already closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the graded \(2+2\) bypass is the correct mainline;
\item the exact concrete Class II-compatible lowest-order branch is Branch B:
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0;
\]
\item the overlap-completed reduced PDE dictionary is explicit:
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O;
\]
\item the finite projected extraction protocol
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_*
\to (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
is explicit;
\item the explicit Class II working branch provides nontrivial witness seeds for
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O.
\]
\end{enumerate}

What remains honestly open:
\begin{enumerate}
\item derive the actual full microscopic transport kernel from the complete TECT Hessian rather than from a reduced working ansatz;
\item compute the actual microscopic values of
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O;
\]
\item verify directly that the complete TECT defect background realizes
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the correct conclusion is not that the full microscopic TECT Dirac problem is completely closed.
The correct conclusion is that the problem has been reduced to a finite and explicit coefficient-extraction computation,
and that the concrete Class II working branch already realizes a nontrivial witness sector.

\section{Final Summary}

The proposed section is mathematically useful, but only after a strict honesty correction.

The heavy Class II mediator does not generate only a single mixed term
\[
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}JK;
\]
rather, the exact quadratic Schur correction is
\[
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}JJ
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(JK+KJ)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}KK.
\]

The current exact mainline is the graded \(2+2\) Branch-B extraction:
\[
OO\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
TD+DT\to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\qquad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
\]
Hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\]

The transport-side coefficients satisfy the exact normalization layer
\[
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O,
\]
so only after overlap specialization may one write
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
\]

Inside the explicit Class II working branch, one may use the canonical branch-level coefficient point
\[
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)},
\]
but this must be labeled as a working-branch realization, not yet the unconditional exact formula of complete TECT.

The precise finite nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\]
equivalently
\[
G_{ij}>0
\iff
g_c\neq 0,\qquad (g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

Therefore the honest current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the finite extraction protocol is explicit,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the concrete Class II working branch provides a nontrivial witness sector,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the full microscopic closure of complete TECT still requires the explicit Hessian extraction of }
\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

\section{Minimal Working Microscopic TECT PDE Consistent with the Closed Constraints}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present stage, we do \emph{not} claim that the full complete TECT action has already been derived from absolute first principles.
What is currently justified is weaker and more precise:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the reduced infrared Dirac-type PDE form is already fixed;
\item the plain scalar Bragg route is insufficient inside the currently safe scalar library;
\item enriched microscopic carrier structure is therefore necessary for the current full-PDE program;
\item the strongest explicit currently available microscopic realization is the refined locked TECT branch coupled to a heavy Class II mediator;
\item the remaining frontier is the explicit coefficient extraction
\[
L(k)\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_*\to (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
\]
equivalently
\[
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\]
from the full background-dependent TECT Hessian.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the correct goal of this section is not to declare the final complete microscopic TECT PDE already finished,
but to record the minimal \emph{working microscopic PDE} and the minimal \emph{final-complete action ansatz}
that are consistent with all already-closed constraints.

\section{1. What is already closed and what is not}

The following points are already structurally closed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:FW_ir_form}
\end{equation}

In the current exact concrete Class II-compatible realization, the sharp reduced form is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{(B)}(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_\theta\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:FW_branchB_form}
\end{equation}

What is \emph{not} yet fully closed is the derivation of the actual coefficient point of the complete microscopic TECT theory:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
}
\label{eq:FW_coeff_open}
\end{equation}
or equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
}
\label{eq:FW_coeff_open2}
\end{equation}
from the full background-dependent TECT Hessian.

Therefore the exact current statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the reduced infrared PDE form is closed,}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the strongest explicit currently available microscopic realization is the refined locked + Class II working branch,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the final complete microscopic TECT action is not yet fully derived unconditionally.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Minimal microscopic working branch}

The strongest explicit microscopic branch currently available is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\label{eq:FW_working_branch}
\end{equation}

Here:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\Psi(x,t)\in \mathbb C^3\) is the condensate triplet field;
\item \(P(x,t)=z(x,t)z(x,t)^\dagger\), \(z^\dagger z=1\), encodes the projector/orientational sector;
\item \(X_i^a(x,t)\) is a heavy Class II internal carrier field;
\item \(L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]\) denotes the refined locked microscopic TECT sector.
\end{itemize}

We do \emph{not} claim that \eqref{eq:FW_working_branch} is already the final complete TECT action.
It is the strongest explicit working microscopic branch in which the full-PDE derivation can currently be pushed concretely.

\section{3. Minimal condensate core}

Inside the minimal local isotropic shell-forming truncation, the condensate core contains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_0[\Psi]
=
\int dt\,d^3x\,
\left[
\frac12 \partial_t\Psi^\dagger\partial_t\Psi
-\frac{\mu^2}{2}\Psi^\dagger\Psi
+\frac Z2 \partial_i\Psi^\dagger\partial_i\Psi
-\frac Y2 (\nabla^2\Psi)^\dagger(\nabla^2\Psi)
-\frac g4 (\Psi^\dagger\Psi)^2
\right].
}
\label{eq:FW_S0}
\end{equation}
Its Euler--Lagrange equation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi.
}
\label{eq:FW_minimal_PDE}
\end{equation}

This is the already-fixed minimal shell-forming condensate PDE.
What the current full-PDE program adds is the enriched carrier structure required to generate the shell-relevant transport coefficients.

\section{4. Heavy Class II mediator elimination}

The heavy mediator satisfies the algebraic equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_i^a
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}
\Bigl(
\alpha_X J_i^a[\Psi]+\beta_X K_i^a[P,\Psi]
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:FW_Xeom}
\end{equation}

Substituting back gives the exact quadratic Schur correction
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X^{(2)}
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a\bigr).
}
\label{eq:FW_Schur_exact}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X^{(2)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}JJ
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(JK+KJ)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}KK.
}
\label{eq:FW_Schur_split}
\end{equation}

Thus it is not correct to retain only a single mixed term
\[
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a
\]
unless one explicitly states that one is working in a reduced mixed-channel truncation.

\section{5. Working microscopic condensate equation}

Varying the working branch with respect to \(\Psi^\dagger\) yields the condensate equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+
\mathcal F_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}
-
\frac{\delta \Delta_X^{(2)}}{\delta \Psi^\dagger}.
}
\label{eq:FW_Psi_full_working}
\end{equation}
After inserting \eqref{eq:FW_Schur_exact}, this may be written more compactly as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+
\mathcal F_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}
-
\frac1{M_X^2}
\frac{\delta}{\delta\Psi^\dagger}
\Bigl[
\bigl(\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a\bigr)
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:FW_Psi_compact}
\end{equation}

If one defines
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_i^a[\Psi,P]
:=
\alpha_X J_i^a[\Psi]+\beta_X K_i^a[P,\Psi],
\label{eq:FW_Jdef}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+
\mathcal F_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}
-
\frac1{M_X^2}
\frac{\delta}{\delta\Psi^\dagger}
\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a\mathcal J_i^a\bigr).
}
\label{eq:FW_PDE_Jcompact}
\end{equation}

This is a legitimate compact working-branch PDE.
However, it should be called the \emph{working microscopic TECT PDE with a heavy Class II carrier},
not the final complete microscopic TECT PDE.

\section{6. Why the Class II branch is justified but not yet unique}

What is currently established is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the plain scalar Bragg route is insufficient in the currently safe scalar library;
\item enriched internal carrier structure must therefore be retained;
\item the refined locked + Class II branch is the strongest explicit currently available working microscopic branch.
\end{enumerate}

What is \emph{not} yet established is that the Class II field is the unique logically possible UV completion.
Indeed, the minimal UV classification still allows multiple effective \((i,a)\)-carrier classes,
of which Class II is the most explicit and currently most useful one.

Therefore the correct language is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is the strongest explicit currently available working branch,}
}
\end{equation}
not
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is already proved to be uniquely and absolutely necessitated.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Relation to the true current frontier}

The actual remaining frontier is not to postulate a deeper ontology,
but to derive the actual transport coefficients from the full background-dependent operator.

The exact finite extraction target is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L(k)\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_*\to (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
}
\label{eq:FW_extract_target}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:FW_block_target}
\end{equation}

At the current sharpest lowest-order realization, the longitudinal sector is on Branch B:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:FW_branchB}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:FW_dictionary}
\end{equation}

Thus the correct conclusion of the present section is not
``Phase I closed from absolute first principles'',
but rather:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the minimal working microscopic PDE and the finite extraction problem are now explicit.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Honest status}

What is already closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the reduced infrared Dirac-type PDE form;
\item the need for enriched carrier structure beyond the plain scalar route;
\item the strongest explicit current working branch \eqref{eq:FW_working_branch};
\item the exact quadratic Schur correction \eqref{eq:FW_Schur_exact}--\eqref{eq:FW_Schur_split};
\item the finite extraction target \eqref{eq:FW_extract_target}--\eqref{eq:FW_block_target}.
\end{enumerate}

What remains honestly open:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual final complete microscopic TECT action;
\item the full background-dependent Hessian extraction of
\[
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O);
\]
\item the direct verification that the complete microscopic TECT theory realizes
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0,\qquad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0)
\]
on the physically relevant defect background.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The proposed section becomes mathematically correct only after a strict honesty correction.

It is not yet justified to say that the full complete microscopic TECT action has been derived
from absolute first principles, nor that the heavy Class II mediator has been proved to be the unique possible completion.

What is currently justified is the following:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The reduced infrared Dirac-type PDE form is already fixed.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The refined locked + heavy Class II sector is the strongest explicit currently available microscopic working branch.}
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{After eliminating the heavy mediator, the exact quadratic correction is }
-\frac1{M_X^2}(\alpha_X J+\beta_X K)(\alpha_X J+\beta_X K),
\text{ containing } JJ,\ JK+KJ,\ KK.
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The true remaining frontier is the explicit coefficient extraction }
L(k)\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_*\to (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
\]

In the current sharpest lowest-order realization,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\qquad \lambda_c\neq 0,
\]
so the reduced Branch-B dictionary is
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\]

Therefore the correct present conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the minimal working microscopic PDE is explicit,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the finite extraction problem is explicit,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the final complete microscopic closure of TECT is still open.}
}
\]

\section{Term-by-Term \(OO\)-Block Longitudinal Audit}

\section{Goal}

The current sharpest blockwise longitudinal problem is to determine the primitive \(OO\)-block coefficient
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2},
\]
equivalently to decide whether
\[
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0.
\]

At the present stage, this is the only remaining transport-level longitudinal question in the current explicit library.

\section{1. Background Hessian and first-order transport layer}

Let the fluctuation field be decomposed as
\[
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta),
\]
with
\[
a\sim T,\qquad \nu\sim O,\qquad \zeta\sim D.
\]
Then the background Hessian has the exact block form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal H_{TT} & \mathcal H_{TO} & \mathcal H_{TD}\\
\mathcal H_{OT} & \mathcal H_{OO} & \mathcal H_{OD}\\
\mathcal H_{DT} & \mathcal H_{DO} & \mathcal H_{DD}
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:OOaudit_full_block}
\end{equation}
Each block admits the worldvolume derivative expansion
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H_{AB}^{(0)}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\mathcal W_{AB}^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
\label{eq:OOaudit_block_expand}
\end{equation}

The shell-relevant first-order transport content is therefore carried by
\[
\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi).
\]

\section{2. Canonical \(OO\)-block decomposition}

In the current explicit library, the orientational diagonal block is recalled in the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y).
}
\label{eq:OOaudit_OOblock}
\end{equation}

This decomposition is to be read term-by-term as follows:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the kinetic piece
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}^{\mathrm{kin}}:=-Z_{O,k}\partial^2;
\]

\item the local potential/background-mass piece
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}:=\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi);
\]

\item the derivative-anisotropy piece
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}:=Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial);
\]

\item the explicit background-induced first-order transport piece
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}^{\mathrm{tr}}:=\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y).
\]
\end{enumerate}

We now audit these four terms against the longitudinal target channel.

\section{3. Longitudinal projector and coefficient expansion}

Project to the tangent doublet bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}Q_B=2,
\]
and let \(\Sigma_a\) be the Pauli basis on \(Q_B\).

Define the \(OO\)-block longitudinal projector
\begin{equation}
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
:=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(
\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\Pi_Q
\bigr).
\label{eq:OOaudit_a3def}
\end{equation}

Its branch-sensitive expansion is
\begin{equation}
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\,\theta'(\xi)
+
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_{3;OO}^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
\label{eq:OOaudit_a3expand}
\end{equation}

The coefficient identification is
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{\parallel;OO}^{(0)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},
\qquad
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
\label{eq:OOaudit_coeff_id}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Primitive longitudinal seed}

For the explicit real \(CP^2\) defect representative, define
\[
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\]
Then the established tangent identities are
\begin{equation}
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\label{eq:OOaudit_Tlinear_zero}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
S_\xi:=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3.
\label{eq:OOaudit_Sxi}
\end{equation}

Therefore the primitive longitudinal transport seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel),\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:OOaudit_primitive_seed}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the Branch-B longitudinal carrier.

\section{5. Term-by-term elimination inside the \(OO\) block}

We now inspect each term in \eqref{eq:OOaudit_OOblock}.

\subsection{5.1 Kinetic term}

The kinetic piece
\[
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
\]
is second order in derivatives and does not by itself produce an odd first-order worldvolume transport tensor of the target form
\[
\theta'(\xi)^m n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]
Hence it does not contribute to the principal \(OO\)-block longitudinal coefficient:
\begin{equation}
a_{3;OO}^{\mathrm{kin}}(\xi)=0
\quad
\text{at the principal first-order transport level.}
\label{eq:OOaudit_kin_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5.2 Potential term}

The background potential term
\[
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
\]
is local and contains no worldvolume derivative.
Therefore it contributes only to zeroth-order local mass/background structure and not to the first-order transport kernel:
\begin{equation}
a_{3;OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)=0
\quad
\text{at the principal transport level.}
\label{eq:OOaudit_pot_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5.3 Derivative-anisotropy term}

The anisotropy piece
\[
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
\]
must be checked more carefully because it contains derivatives.

However, in the solved lowest-order realization, the reflection-symmetry and projector-commutator audit shows that the linear Branch-A longitudinal monomial
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
\]
is forbidden, while the first allowed longitudinal monomial is
\[
\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}=0.
}
\label{eq:OOaudit_ell1_zero}
\end{equation}
In particular, the derivative-anisotropy term does not generate a nonzero Branch-A coefficient in the current solved lowest-order class:
\begin{equation}
a_{3;OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi)
\text{ does not contribute a nonzero }
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}.
\label{eq:OOaudit_gradani_no_branchA}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5.4 Transport term}

After eliminating the kinetic, potential, and Branch-A-forbidden contributions, the only surviving leading longitudinal carrier inside the \(OO\) block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_{OO}.
}
\label{eq:OOaudit_T_only}
\end{equation}

Its shell-relevant traceless longitudinal projection is precisely the primitive channel
\eqref{eq:OOaudit_primitive_seed}.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_{OO}
\;\Rightarrow\;
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:OOaudit_T_to_lambda}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Final \(OO\)-block verdict}

Combining the previous steps, the global \(OO\)-block longitudinal result is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:OOaudit_global_result}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_{3;OO}^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:OOaudit_a3final}
\end{equation}

Thus, in the current solved lowest-order class, the \(OO\)-block does not realize Branch A and carries only the primitive Branch-B longitudinal seed.

\section{7. Reduced longitudinal coefficient}

After shell localization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:OOaudit_lambda_parallel}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:OOaudit_I3}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_{c;OO}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:OOaudit_lambda_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Practical finite test}

Therefore the entire Gate-2 longitudinal problem in the current explicit library reduces to the single finite extraction
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?.
}
\label{eq:OOaudit_single_test}
\end{equation}

If yes, then
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\]
immediately follows because \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\).

\section{9. Honest status}

What is proved at the present stage is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(OO\)-block is the natural primitive longitudinal candidate block;
\item the linear Branch-A coefficient vanishes in the solved lowest-order realization:
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}=0;
\]
\item the only surviving leading \(OO\)-block longitudinal carrier is \(\mathcal T_{OO}\);
\item therefore
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}
\]
is the sharp current transport-level target.
\end{enumerate}

What is still not yet fully inserted is the literal term-by-term evaluation of the complete final microscopic TECT operator that yields the numerical/symbolic value of \(\lambda_{c;OO}\).
So the frontier is no longer structural.
It is the explicit finite extraction \(\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\).

\section{Final Summary}

The \(OO\)-block longitudinal audit is now reduced to a single primitive transport coefficient.

The exact orientational diagonal block is organized as
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y).
\]

In the solved lowest-order realization,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,
\]
because the linear longitudinal monomial
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
\]
is forbidden, while the first allowed longitudinal traceless seed is
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel),\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]

Hence the kinetic term, the local potential term, and the Branch-A-forbidden linear anisotropy sector do not provide the leading longitudinal carrier.
The only surviving leading \(OO\)-block source is
\[
\mathcal T_{OO},
\]
and therefore
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
\]

After shell localization,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_{c;OO}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]

Therefore the entire current Gate-2 longitudinal problem is reduced to the single finite question
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?.
}
\]

What remains open is not the structure of the argument.
It is the explicit insertion of the final complete microscopic TECT operator into the \(OO\)-block transport extraction.
