\section{Schur-Corrected Microscopic Source Sheet for the \(OO\)-Block Longitudinal Carrier}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present stage, the longitudinal carrier problem is no longer a broad structural classification problem.
It has reduced to the explicit source audit of the \(OO\)-block transport operator.

What is already structurally fixed is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the heavy Class II correction decomposes into
\[
JJ,\qquad JK,\qquad KK;
\]
\item the shell-adapted leading branch has
\[
J\ \text{purely longitudinal},\qquad K\ \text{purely transverse};
\]
\item therefore the primitive longitudinal \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet can survive only through the \(JJ\)-sector at principal shell order.
\end{enumerate}

What is not yet fully frozen is the exact convention-level coupling prefactor of the resulting longitudinal coefficient,
because different working notes currently use two notationally inequivalent normalizations.

\section{1. Starting point: exact Schur decomposition}

The heavy-mediated correction to the effective microscopic operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}
(\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K)
(\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K)^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_Schur_exact}
\end{equation}
Hence the transport contribution decomposes channelwise as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X
=
\Delta_X^{JJ}
+
\Delta_X^{JK}
+
\Delta_X^{KK},
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_channel_split}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{align}
\Delta_X^{JJ} &=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal J\mathcal J^\dagger,
\label{eq:OOsheet_DJJ}
\\
\Delta_X^{JK} &=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\mathcal J\mathcal K^\dagger+\mathcal K\mathcal J^\dagger\bigr),
\label{eq:OOsheet_DJK}
\\
\Delta_X^{KK} &=
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal K\mathcal K^\dagger.
\label{eq:OOsheet_DKK}
\end{align}

Thus the \(OO\)-block first-order transport term may be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_{OO}
=
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(\mathrm{ref})}
+
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(JJ)}
+
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(JK)}
+
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(KK)}.
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_TOO_split}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Shell-adapted leading branch forms}

At the current explicit leading shell level, the intervalley tensors are taken in the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,j^a\,(\Sigma_3)_r
+
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a,\mathrm{null}},
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_Jlead}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,k^a
\Bigl[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}(\Sigma_2)_r
\Bigr]
+
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a,\mathrm{null}}.
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_Klead}
\end{equation}

Therefore, at principal shell order,
\[
J\sim \Sigma_3,
\qquad
K\sim \Lambda_E^{(0)}\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O^{(0)}\Sigma_2.
\]

\section{3. Longitudinal projector}

Project to the tangent doublet space \(Q_B\) and define the \(OO\)-block longitudinal scalar
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(
\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)
\bigr),
\qquad
V^\mu_{OO}:=\Pi_Q\,\mathbb H^\mu_{1,OO}\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_a3}
\end{equation}

Its branch-sensitive expansion is
\begin{equation}
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\theta'(\xi)^3
+\cdots,
\qquad
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
\label{eq:OOsheet_branch_expansion}
\end{equation}

In the solved current lowest-order realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0,
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_branchA_absent}
\end{equation}
so the actual longitudinal target is the primitive Branch-B coefficient
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
\]

\section{4. Source-by-source longitudinal audit}

Decompose
\begin{equation}
a_{3;OO}
=
a_{3;OO}^{(\mathrm{ref})}
+
a_{3;OO}^{(JJ)}
+
a_{3;OO}^{(JK)}
+
a_{3;OO}^{(KK)}.
\label{eq:OOsheet_a3split}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4.1 Refined locked core}

The refined locked core may in principle contribute background-dependent transport terms,
but in the current solved library it does not provide an allowed principal Branch-A longitudinal seed.
Thus, at the sharpest present stage, it is not the distinguished carrier of the primitive odd longitudinal singlet.

So the current longitudinal frontier is not a general ``refined core'' question.
It is the explicit primitive source audit of the Schur-generated carrier channels.

\subsection{4.2 \(JJ\)-sector}

Because \(J\) is purely shell-normal and aligned with \(\Sigma_3\),
the \(JJ\)-sector is axial only at principal shell order.
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(JJ)}\propto m_3,
\qquad
\alpha^{(JJ)}=0,
\qquad
\beta^{(JJ)}=0.
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_JJ_axial}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}^{(JJ)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c^{(JJ)}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_a3JJ}
\end{equation}
is allowed and is the unique principal longitudinal channel.

\subsection{4.3 \(JK\)-sector}

At the naive local Hermitian level,
\[
\Sigma_3(\Lambda_E\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O\Sigma_2)
+
(\Lambda_E\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3=0
\]
by Pauli anticommutation.
At the derivative-resolved shell level, the mixed sector rotates into transverse Pauli directions,
since
\[
\Sigma_3\Sigma_1=i\Sigma_2,
\qquad
\Sigma_3\Sigma_2=-i\Sigma_1.
\]
Therefore the mixed channel feeds the transverse coefficients only:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(JK)}=0
\qquad
\text{at principal shell order.}
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_cparJKzero}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}^{(JK)}(\xi)=0
\qquad
\text{at principal longitudinal shell order.}
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_a3JKzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4.4 \(KK\)-sector}

Since the \(K\)-sector itself carries no leading \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet component,
its quadratic self-channel remains in the transverse family at the shell-relevant leading order.
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(KK)}=0
\qquad
\text{at the primitive shell-relevant longitudinal level,}
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_cparKKzero}
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}^{(KK)}(\xi)=0
\qquad
\text{at principal longitudinal shell order.}
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_a3KKzero}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Principal classification theorem}

Collecting the previous results,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
a_{3;OO}^{(JJ)}(\xi)
+
\text{higher/nonleading terms},
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_a3localized}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}^{(JJ)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c^{(JJ)}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3+\cdots,
\qquad
a_{3;OO}^{(JK)}=0,
\qquad
a_{3;OO}^{(KK)}=0
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_main_localization}
\end{equation}
at principal longitudinal shell order.

Therefore the unique principal \(OO\)-block longitudinal source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_unique_source}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Reduced longitudinal coefficient}

After shell localization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\lambda_{c;OO}\equiv \lambda_c^{(JJ)}
\quad
\text{at principal shell order.}
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_lambda_reduced}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire current longitudinal carrier problem reduces to the single finite question
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0\ ?.
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_single_question}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest convention mismatch}

Here one must distinguish two layers.

\paragraph{Layer A: structural source classification.}
This layer is already closed:
\[
JJ\ \text{is the unique principal longitudinal source},
\qquad
JK,\ KK\ \text{do not contribute to }c_\parallel
\]
at principal shell order.

\paragraph{Layer B: explicit coupling-prefactor normalization.}
At this layer, the current note package contains two different working normalizations:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a channel-decomposed Bloch-renormalization form
\[
\Delta\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{KK},
\]
which reduces structurally to a \(JJ\)-only longitudinal channel;

\item a one-mediator canonical shell-projection form
\[
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}C_\parallel.
\]
\end{enumerate}

These two expressions are not yet manifestly identical at the notation level.
Therefore the exact coupling prefactor of \(\lambda_{c;OO}\) is not yet fully frozen across all working-note conventions.

What is robustly true is only the convention-free statement:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the principal longitudinal source is unique and localized to the allowed longitudinal channel.}
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_conventionfree}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Practical execution target}

The correct next direct execution is therefore not another structural theorem.
It is to evaluate the actual projected Bloch normalization entering the unique longitudinal source,
for example through either of the equivalent routes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{OO}\to a_{3;OO}(\xi)\to \lambda_{c;OO},
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_routeA}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel
=
P_*\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*)P_*
\to
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel).
}
\label{eq:OOsheet_routeB}
\end{equation}

So the remaining frontier is a finite microscopic insertion problem, not a missing conceptual structure.

\section{Final Summary}

The \(OO\)-block longitudinal transport operator admits the Schur-corrected source decomposition
\[
\mathcal T_{OO}
=
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(\mathrm{ref})}
+
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(JJ)}
+
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(JK)}
+
\mathcal T_{OO}^{(KK)}.
\]

At the current shell-adapted leading branch,
\[
J\sim \Sigma_3
\quad\text{(longitudinal)},
\qquad
K\sim \Lambda_E^{(0)}\Sigma_1+\Lambda_O^{(0)}\Sigma_2
\quad\text{(transverse)}.
\]

Therefore the principal longitudinal source classification is:
\[
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}^{(JJ)}\neq 0\ \text{is allowed},
\qquad
a_{3;OO}^{(JK)}=0,
\qquad
a_{3;OO}^{(KK)}=0
\quad
\text{at principal shell order}.
}
\]

Equivalently, the primitive \(OO\)-block longitudinal coefficient localizes to the \(JJ\)-sector:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\equiv \lambda_c^{(JJ)}
\quad
\text{at principal shell order}.
}
\]

Hence the reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
}
\]
and the remaining microscopic longitudinal problem is the single finite test
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0\ ?.
}
\]

What is fully closed:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the principal source classification }(JJ\text{ only})\text{ is closed.}
}
\]

What is not yet fully frozen:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the exact coupling-prefactor normalization of }\lambda_{c;OO}
\text{ across all current note conventions.}
}
\]

Thus the true next step is not another structural theorem,
but the explicit projected Bloch evaluation of the unique longitudinal source.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Convention Audit for \texorpdfstring{$\Lambda_c^{JJ}$}{Lambda c JJ} versus \texorpdfstring{$C_\parallel$}{Cparallel}}

\section{Short explanation}

The current note package contains two different longitudinal normalizations.

One normalization is the exact Class-II renormalization of the reduced locked coefficients:
\[
\Delta\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{KK}.
\]
The other normalization is the Branch-B one-mediator Bloch calibration:
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}C_\parallel I_3.
\]

These are not manifestly the same definition.
Therefore the correct task is not to assert equality immediately, but to separate
what is convention-free from what still depends on the chosen normalization layer.

\section{1. Exact channel-renormalization layer}

In the exact Class-II renormalization notes, the reduced locked coefficients are split as
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{ref}}+\Delta\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=\alpha^{\mathrm{ref}}+\Delta\alpha,
\qquad
\beta=\beta^{\mathrm{ref}}+\Delta\beta,
\]
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{KK}.
}
\label{eq:audit_dlambda_exact}
\end{equation}
The channel overlaps are defined by projected Pauli traces:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_c^{UV}
:=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\Bigl(
\sigma_3\,P_*(\hat n_\ell\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{UV}(k_*))P_*
\Bigr),
\qquad
(U,V)\in\{(J,J),(J,K),(K,K)\}.
}
\label{eq:audit_LcJJ_def}
\end{equation}

So \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\) is a transport-side projected Bloch-derivative invariant
attached specifically to the \(JJ\) channel.

\section{2. Principal source classification}

Independently of normalization, the current source-classification notes imply:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ\text{ alone probes only the longitudinal-type shell singlet,}
}
\label{eq:audit_JJ_long_only}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ\text{ alone does not generate }(g_E,g_O),
\qquad
JK/KK\text{ are required for the transverse pair.}
}
\label{eq:audit_JJ_not_trans}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, at principal longitudinal shell order,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_c^{JK}=0,
\qquad
\Lambda_c^{KK}=0
\quad
\text{(or, more precisely, they do not contribute to the principal allowed longitudinal slot).}
}
\label{eq:audit_JKKK_zero_long}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact channel formula reduces structurally to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med},\parallel)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}
}
\label{eq:audit_dlambda_JJ_only}
\end{equation}
at principal longitudinal shell order.

This part is convention-free and already closed.

\section{3. Branch-B overlap-completed layer}

A different family of notes uses the Branch-B reduced dictionary
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3,
\qquad
I_3=I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:audit_branchB_dict}
\end{equation}
Then, in the one-mediator shell-projected calibration,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}C_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:audit_lamc_Cpar}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}C_\parallel I_3.
}
\label{eq:audit_lambda_Cpar}
\end{equation}

Moreover,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X I_3}
\Bigl[
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}
-
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:audit_Cpar_diag}
\end{equation}
hence \(C_\parallel\) is a Bloch-calibration constant extracted from the diagonal difference
of a projected shell matrix.

Thus \(C_\parallel\) lives at a different explicit normalization layer from \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\).

\section{4. Why the two formulas cannot yet be identified unconditionally}

Comparing \eqref{eq:audit_dlambda_JJ_only} and \eqref{eq:audit_lambda_Cpar},
one is tempted to write
\begin{equation}
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}
\stackrel{?}{=}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}C_\parallel I_3.
\label{eq:audit_tempting_eq}
\end{equation}
If this were justified, it would imply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
\frac{2\alpha_X}{\beta_X I_3}\,\Lambda_c^{JJ}.
}
\label{eq:audit_formal_relation}
\end{equation}

However, this step is not yet licensed by the current notes alone.
To make \eqref{eq:audit_formal_relation} rigorous, one would need all of the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(\lambda_\parallel\) appearing in \eqref{eq:audit_dlambda_JJ_only} and \eqref{eq:audit_lambda_Cpar}
must be exactly the same mediated contribution, not one total coefficient and one branch-reduced coefficient;

\item the reference/core contribution must either vanish or be subtracted in the same convention:
\[
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{ref}}=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\lambda_\parallel\to \Delta\lambda_\parallel;
\]

\item the \(JJ\)-trace object
\[
P_*(\hat n_\ell\mathfrak D_\ell^{JJ}(k_*))P_*
\]
must be shown explicitly to equal, after overlap completion and basis normalization,
the diagonal-difference object
\[
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}-(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22};
\]

\item the same shell overlap normalization \(I_3\) and the same sign conventions must be used on both sides.
\end{enumerate}

The currently uploaded notes do not yet contain this explicit identification chain.
Therefore \eqref{eq:audit_formal_relation} is at present only a \emph{candidate conversion formula},
not a proved identity.

\section{5. What is actually proved right now}

The following statement is rigorous and convention-free:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{At principal longitudinal shell order, the unique allowed source is the }JJ\text{ channel.}
}
\label{eq:audit_rigorous1}
\end{equation}

Hence the mediated longitudinal coefficient is controlled by a single scalar,
which may be represented in different conventions as:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\): projected Pauli-trace of the \(JJ\) derivative block;

\item \(\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\): primitive longitudinal \(OO\)-block coefficient;

\item \(C_\parallel\): one-mediator Bloch calibration constant of the Branch-B shell reduction.
\end{enumerate}

So the correct current statement is not
\[
\Lambda_c^{JJ}=C_\parallel
\]
but rather
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_c^{JJ},\ \lambda_c^{(JJ)},\ C_\parallel
\text{ are three longitudinal calibration representatives belonging to different note conventions.}
}
\label{eq:audit_representatives}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Safe canonical choice going forward}

To eliminate the ambiguity, the safest master definition is to define the mediated longitudinal coefficient directly by the projected Bloch derivative:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}
:=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\Bigl(
\sigma_3\,P_*(\hat n_i\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(\mathrm{med})}(k_*))P_*
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:audit_master_def}
\end{equation}

Then define the conversion quantities only \emph{from} this master coefficient:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_c^{JJ}
:=
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X^2}\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med},JJ)},
}
\label{eq:audit_master_to_Lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
:=
-\frac{2M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X I_3}\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}.
}
\label{eq:audit_master_to_Cpar}
\end{equation}

With this convention, any future equality between \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\) and \(C_\parallel\)
must emerge as a derived conversion identity, not as an assumption.

\section{7. Honest final verdict}

Therefore the convention audit yields the following precise verdict:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Source classification: closed.}
}
\label{eq:audit_closed_source}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ\text{ is the unique principal longitudinal source.}
}
\label{eq:audit_closed_source2}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Normalization equivalence between }\Lambda_c^{JJ}\text{ and }C_\parallel\text{: not yet proved.}
}
\label{eq:audit_not_closed_norm}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The remaining task is an explicit same-projector same-basis same-overlap conversion computation.}
}
\label{eq:audit_remaining_task}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The uploaded notes contain two different longitudinal normalizations.

The first is the exact Class-II channel-renormalization form
\[
\Delta\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{KK},
\]
where \(\Lambda_c^{UV}\) is defined by projected Pauli traces of derivative blocks.

The second is the Branch-B one-mediator shell-calibration form
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}C_\parallel I_3,
\qquad
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}C_\parallel,
\]
where \(C_\parallel\) is extracted from the diagonal difference of the projected shell matrix.

What is rigorously closed is the source classification:
\[
JJ\text{ is the unique principal longitudinal source,}
\qquad
JK,\ KK \text{ do not contribute to the principal allowed longitudinal slot.}
\]

Therefore the exact channel formula reduces structurally to
\[
\Delta\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med},\parallel)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}.
\]

However, the present notes do not yet prove that
\[
\Lambda_c^{JJ}
=
\frac{\beta_X I_3}{2\alpha_X}C_\parallel
\]
or any equivalent relation, because the two objects are introduced at different normalization layers
and have not yet been written in the same projector/basis/overlap convention.

Thus the correct present verdict is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{source classification is closed,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{normalization equivalence between }\Lambda_c^{JJ}\text{ and }C_\parallel\text{ is still open.}
}
\]

The safest canonical next step is to define
\[
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\Bigl(
\sigma_3\,P_*(\hat n_i\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(\mathrm{med})}(k_*))P_*
\Bigr)
\]
as the master longitudinal scalar and derive both \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\) and \(C_\parallel\) from it.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Master-Object Unification of \texorpdfstring{$\Lambda_c^{JJ}$}{Lambda c JJ}, \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_{c;OO}$}{lambda c OO}, and \texorpdfstring{$C_\parallel$}{Cparallel}}

\section{Short explanation}

The safest way to remove the current notation drift is to avoid identifying
\[
\Lambda_c^{JJ},\qquad \lambda_{c;OO},\qquad C_\parallel
\]
directly.

Instead, one first defines a single master projected longitudinal scalar from the mediated Bloch operator,
and only afterwards introduces the three note-dependent calibration variables as derived quantities.

This removes the ambiguity between the channel-renormalization notes and the Branch-B one-mediator shell-calibration notes.

\section{1. Master projected Bloch longitudinal scalar}

Let
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{med})}
:=
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(\mathrm{med})}(k)\Big|_{k=k_*},
\qquad
K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}:=\hat n_i K_i^{(\mathrm{med})}.
\]
Define the exact mediated longitudinal master scalar by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}
:=
\frac12\Tr\!\Bigl(
\sigma_3\,P_*K_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}P_*
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:master_lambda_med}
\end{equation}

This is the common projector-trace object underlying all current longitudinal notations.

\section{2. Channel-renormalization convention}

In the exact Class-II channel-renormalization notes, one writes
\[
K_\ell
=
\left.\partial_{k_\ell}H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}
-
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{JJ}(k_*)
-
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{JK}(k_*)
-
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{KK}(k_*),
\]
and hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\lambda_\parallel^{\rm ref}
+
\Delta\lambda_\parallel,
\]
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{KK}.
}
\label{eq:master_dlambda_channels}
\end{equation}
The channel overlap is defined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_c^{UV}
:=
\frac12\Tr\!\Bigl(
\sigma_3\,P_*(\hat n_\ell\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{UV}(k_*))P_*
\Bigr),
\qquad
(U,V)\in\{(J,J),(J,K),(K,K)\}.
}
\label{eq:master_LambdaUV_def}
\end{equation}

At principal longitudinal shell order, the source classification is already fixed:
\[
JJ\ \text{is the unique allowed longitudinal source},
\qquad
JK,\ KK\ \text{do not contribute to the principal allowed longitudinal slot}.
\]
Therefore the structural reduction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}
=
\Delta\lambda_\parallel^{(\parallel)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}.
}
\label{eq:master_lambda_from_LambdaJJ}
\end{equation}

Thus \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\) is the channel-renormalization representative of the master longitudinal scalar.

\section{3. Branch-B transport convention}

In the Branch-B transport notes, the primitive longitudinal seed is
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel),\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
so the reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:master_branchB_lambdac}
\end{equation}

Under the current \(OO\)-candidate interpretation,
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2},
\]
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3,
\qquad
I_3:=I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:master_lambda_from_lambdaOO}
\end{equation}

Thus \(\lambda_{c;OO}\) is the transport-side primitive longitudinal representative of the same Branch-B longitudinal slot.

\section{4. One-mediator shell-calibration convention}

In the one-mediator shell-projected calibration notes,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}C_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:master_lambdaOO_Cpar}
\end{equation}
and equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}C_\parallel I_3.
}
\label{eq:master_lambda_Cpar}
\end{equation}

Therefore \(C_\parallel\) is the shell-calibration representative of the same longitudinal Branch-B coefficient, but after a different normalization choice.

\section{5. Unified dictionary}

Equations \eqref{eq:master_lambda_from_LambdaJJ}, \eqref{eq:master_lambda_from_lambdaOO}, and \eqref{eq:master_lambda_Cpar}
show that the clean unified hierarchy is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}
\longleftrightarrow
\Lambda_c^{JJ}
\quad\text{(channel-renormalization convention)},
}
\label{eq:master_dict1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}
\longleftrightarrow
\lambda_{c;OO}
\quad\text{(primitive Branch-B transport convention)},
}
\label{eq:master_dict2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}
\longleftrightarrow
C_\parallel
\quad\text{(one-mediator shell-calibration convention)}.
}
\label{eq:master_dict3}
\end{equation}

So the three variables should not be treated as primary objects of equal status.
The primary object is the master Bloch scalar \(\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}\).

\section{6. Conditional conversion formulas}

If one assumes that all three note families refer to the same pure mediated longitudinal contribution,
with the same projector, the same valley basis, and the same overlap normalization,
then one may combine the formulas to obtain

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
\frac{2\,\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}}{I_3},
}
\label{eq:master_conv_lambdaOO}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_c^{JJ}
=
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X^2}\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})},
}
\label{eq:master_conv_LJJ}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
-\frac{2M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X I_3}\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}.
}
\label{eq:master_conv_Cpar}
\end{equation}

Under these same assumptions, one gets the candidate conversion laws
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}C_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:master_conv_lambdaOO_Cpar_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
\frac{2\alpha_X}{\beta_X I_3}\Lambda_c^{JJ},
}
\label{eq:master_candidate_conversion}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2 I_3}\Lambda_c^{JJ}.
}
\label{eq:master_candidate_conversion2}
\end{equation}

However, \eqref{eq:master_candidate_conversion}--\eqref{eq:master_candidate_conversion2}
must be labeled explicitly as \emph{conditional conversion formulas},
because the uploaded notes do not yet provide the fully explicit same-projector same-basis same-overlap derivation linking the three conventions.

\section{7. Finite-sum realization of the master scalar}

The carrier-side longitudinal audit notes already provide an explicit finite harmonic representative:
\[
V_\parallel^{(JJ)}=-\Gamma_J M,
\qquad
m_3=\frac12(M_{11}-M_{22}),
\]
with the finite sum
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\Big(
\overline{c_{1,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{1,G'}^{(-)}
-
\overline{c_{2,G}^{(+)}}
\,c_{2,G'}^{(-)}
\Big)
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*+G-G').
}
\label{eq:master_finite_sum}
\end{equation}

This is the explicit computational realization of the longitudinal master slot.
If
\[
m_3\neq0,
\]
then
\[
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
\]

Hence the remaining microscopic longitudinal frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the literal computation of this projected finite harmonic quantity from the refined locked Bloch data.

\section{8. Safe canonical convention going forward}

To avoid further notation drift, the safest convention is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item define the master longitudinal scalar by \eqref{eq:master_lambda_med};
\item define \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\) only through \eqref{eq:master_conv_LJJ};
\item define \(\lambda_{c;OO}\) only through \eqref{eq:master_conv_lambdaOO};
\item define \(C_\parallel\) only through \eqref{eq:master_conv_Cpar}.
\end{enumerate}

Then any future equality among \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\), \(\lambda_{c;OO}\), and \(C_\parallel\)
becomes a derived conversion identity rather than an assumed identification.

\section{9. Honest final verdict}

The current notation audit yields the following exact conclusion:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Source classification is closed: }JJ\text{ is the unique principal longitudinal source.}
}
\label{eq:master_verdict1}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_c^{JJ},\ \lambda_{c;OO},\ C_\parallel
\text{ are three convention-dependent representatives of one longitudinal master slot.}

\label{eq:master_verdict2}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Their full explicit conversion is not yet unconditional, because the same-projector same-basis same-overlap derivation is still unwritten.}
}
\label{eq:master_verdict3}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The remaining task is a finite projected Bloch evaluation of the master scalar } \lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}.
}
\label{eq:master_verdict4}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The safest unification of the current longitudinal notations is to introduce the master projected Bloch scalar

\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{med})}
:=

\section{Harmonic-Data Unification of the Longitudinal \texorpdfstring{$JJ$}{JJ} Slot}

\section{Short explanation}

The safest way to remove the remaining notation drift is to define a single
longitudinal master scalar directly from the harmonic finite-sum realization of the
pure-\(JJ\) Class-II transport contribution.

The key point is that the source classification is already closed:
the principal longitudinal slot is carried only by the axial \(JJ\)-sector,
while \(JK\) and \(KK\) remain transverse-family at principal longitudinal shell order.

Hence the true primary object is not
\[
\Lambda_c^{JJ},\qquad \lambda_{c;OO},\qquad C_\parallel
\]
separately,
but one unique longitudinal master scalar extracted from the same harmonic data.

\section{1. Exact Class-II longitudinal master scalar}

The pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal Class-II contribution is already reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}=-\Gamma_J\,m_3.
}
\label{eq:masterII_start}
\end{equation}
At the same time, the finite harmonic extraction gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_3
=
-\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2\Gamma_J}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:masterII_m3}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:masterII_exact}
\end{equation}

We now define the pure longitudinal harmonic master slot by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}
:=
v_\parallel^{(II)}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_def}
\end{equation}

This is the cleanest convention-free representative of the pure \(JJ\) longitudinal channel.

\section{2. Canonical branch reduction of the harmonic input}

In the current canonical branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto
\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_VJJ}
\end{equation}
Moreover, the valley-mixing scalar and the shell-normal \(J\)-bias are given by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_Delta00}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_Lstar}
\end{equation}

Hence the dominant one-mode approximation to the longitudinal master scalar is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_{\parallel,0}^{(JJ)}
=
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_dominant}
\end{equation}

Thus the pure longitudinal slot is controlled by the finite harmonic data
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0),E_-(0),U_\parallel,m_\parallel,A_{G_*},R_N).
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_finite_data}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Total longitudinal column versus pure Class-II slot}

The total longitudinal column is not identical to the pure Class-II contribution.
In the current Bloch-operator working truncation one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}^{\,3}_\parallel
+
v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_total_column}
\end{equation}
In the one-step scalar spectator truncation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}=0,
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_sp_zero}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}^{\,3}_\parallel
+
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_total_reduced}
\end{equation}

Therefore it is crucial to distinguish:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \emph{pure mediated/Class-II longitudinal slot}
\[
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)};
\]

\item the \emph{total longitudinal coefficient}
\[
v_\parallel.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Any exact conversion formula among \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\), \(\lambda_{c;OO}\), and \(C_\parallel\)
must specify clearly which of these two layers is being represented.

\section{4. Channel-renormalization representative}

In the exact channel-renormalization convention, the mediated longitudinal correction is written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta\lambda_\parallel^{(\parallel)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ},
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_LambdaJJ_layer}
\end{equation}
because the \(JJ\)-channel is the unique principal longitudinal source.

Therefore the channel-renormalization representative of the master slot is defined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_c^{JJ}
:=
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X^2}\,
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_LambdaJJ_def}
\end{equation}

This is the clean way to interpret \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\):
it is not an independent primitive object, but the \(JJ\)-channel normalization of the same master scalar.

\section{5. Primitive Branch-B transport representative}

In the Branch-B reduced transport convention,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
I_3:=I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_BranchB_dict}
\end{equation}
For the \(OO\)-candidate primitive slot, this is written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_lambdaOO_layer}
\end{equation}

Hence, if one wishes to use the pure Class-II master slot as the primitive longitudinal representative,
the natural definition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}^{(JJ)}
:=
\frac{2}{I_3}\,
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_lambdaOO_def}
\end{equation}

So \(\lambda_{c;OO}^{(JJ)}\) is the primitive Branch-B transport normalization of the same harmonic master scalar.

\section{6. One-mediator shell-calibration representative}

The one-mediator shell-calibration notes write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}C_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_Cpar_layer1}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}C_\parallel I_3.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_Cpar_layer2}
\end{equation}

Therefore the shell-calibration representative of the same master slot is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel^{(JJ)}
:=
-\frac{2M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X I_3}\,
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_Cpar_def}
\end{equation}

Again, this should be understood as a derived definition from the master scalar,
not as an independent primary coefficient.

\section{7. Unified dictionary}

The correct unification is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}
\longleftrightarrow
\Lambda_c^{JJ}
\quad\text{(channel-renormalization representative)},
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_dict1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}
\longleftrightarrow
\lambda_{c;OO}^{(JJ)}
\quad\text{(primitive Branch-B transport representative)},
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_dict2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}
\longleftrightarrow
C_\parallel^{(JJ)}
\quad\text{(one-mediator shell-calibration representative)}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_dict3}
\end{equation}

Hence \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\), \(\lambda_{c;OO}\), and \(C_\parallel\) should not be treated as three separate physical quantities.
They are three convention-dependent representatives of one and the same harmonic longitudinal slot.

\section{8. Conditional conversion formulas}

Once the master definition is adopted, the formal conversions are immediate:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}^{(JJ)}
=
\frac{2}{I_3}\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)},
\qquad
\Lambda_c^{JJ}
=
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X^2}\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)},
\qquad
C_\parallel^{(JJ)}
=
-\frac{2M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X I_3}\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_all_conversions}
\end{equation}

Combining them gives the candidate pairwise conversion laws
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel^{(JJ)}
=
\frac{2\alpha_X}{\beta_X I_3}\Lambda_c^{JJ},
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_pair_conv1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}^{(JJ)}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2 I_3}\Lambda_c^{JJ},
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_pair_conv2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}^{(JJ)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}C_\parallel^{(JJ)}.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_pair_conv3}
\end{equation}

However, these must still be labeled as \emph{master-convention conversion formulas}.
They become note-by-note identities only after one verifies that the compared notes are indeed referring to the same pure mediated contribution and not to different total/reduced/truncated coefficient layers.

\section{9. Practical finite sufficient condition}

The master scalar formulation now makes the actual longitudinal survival test transparent.

Since
\[
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}
=
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr),
\]
and
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto
\alpha_X L_* A_{G_*},
\]
a practical sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_sufficient}
\end{equation}

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_ultramin}
\end{equation}

Thus the longitudinal frontier is now reduced to a finite matrix-element insertion problem in the harmonic master data.

\section{10. Honest final verdict}

The genuinely primary longitudinal quantity is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}
=
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:Lmaster_final_primary}
\end{equation}

What is fully closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(JJ\) is the unique principal longitudinal source;
\item \(m_3\), \(v_\parallel^{(II)}\), \(\Delta_{00}\), and \(L_*\) all belong to one finite harmonic-data pipeline;
\item \(\Lambda_c^{JJ}\), \(\lambda_{c;OO}\), and \(C_\parallel\) can all be defined consistently from this same master scalar.
\end{enumerate}

What is still honest-open:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual microscopic numerical/symbolic insertion of
\[
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel,\ A_{G_*},\ R_N;
\]
\item the exact note-by-note identification of every historical formula with this unified master convention.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The cleanest resolution of the remaining longitudinal notation drift is to introduce the pure-\(JJ\) harmonic master scalar
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}
:=
v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr).
}
\]

This scalar is the unique principal Class-II longitudinal slot because the source classification is already closed:
\[
\boxed{
JJ\text{ is the unique principal longitudinal source,}
\qquad
JK,\ KK\text{ do not contribute to the principal longitudinal slot.}
}
\]

In the current canonical branch,
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto
\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
u_\parallel=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\Sigma_3U_\parallel),
\]
and
\[
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-.
\]
Therefore the longitudinal frontier is completely reduced to finite harmonic data.

The three previously competing notations are then understood as derived representatives of the same master scalar:
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_c^{JJ}
=
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X^2}\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}^{(JJ)}
=
\frac{2}{I_3}\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_\parallel^{(JJ)}
=
-\frac{2M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X I_3}\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_c^{JJ},\ \lambda_{c;OO},\ C_\parallel
\text{ are not three independent physical coefficients.}
}
\]
They are three convention-dependent representatives of one and the same longitudinal harmonic slot.

The practical sufficient condition for longitudinal survival is
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\]
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,\qquad
L_*\neq 0,\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore the remaining open part is no longer structural.
It is the explicit microscopic insertion of the finite harmonic data
\[
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel,\ A_{G_*},\ R_N.

\section{Direct Finite Extraction of \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00} and \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{L*} in the Canonical Locked Basis}

\section{Short explanation}

The remaining carrier-side longitudinal problem has been reduced to a literal finite \(2\times2\) matrix audit.
The only nontrivial longitudinal scalars are
\[
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\]
where \(\eta_\pm\) are the normalized low eigenvectors of the valley blocks \(E_\pm(0)\), and
\[
u_\parallel=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\Sigma_3U_\parallel),
\qquad
U_\parallel=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0).
\]

\section{1. Explicit valley blocks}

Write the two valley-diagonal projected blocks as general Hermitian matrices:
\begin{equation}
E_+(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_+ & c_+\\
\overline{c_+} & b_+
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
E_-(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_- & c_-\\
\overline{c_-} & b_-
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Epm_general_final}
\end{equation}
with
\[
a_\pm,b_\pm\in\mathbb R,
\qquad
c_\pm\in\mathbb C.
\]

Define
\begin{equation}
t_\pm:=\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2},
\qquad
d_\pm:=\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2},
\qquad
\rho_\pm:=|c_\pm|.
\label{eq:tdrho_def_final}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
E_\pm(0)
=
t_\pm\mathbf 1_2
+
d_\pm\Sigma_3
+
(\Re c_\pm)\Sigma_1
-
(\Im c_\pm)\Sigma_2.
\label{eq:Epm_pauli_final}
\end{equation}

Hence the nontrivial Bloch vector of each valley block is
\[
\mathbf h_\pm=(\Re c_\pm,\,-\Im c_\pm,\,d_\pm).
\]

\section{2. Low eigenvalues and normalized low eigenvectors}

The two eigenvalues of \(E_\pm(0)\) are
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low/high})}
=
t_\pm\mp R_\pm,
\qquad
R_\pm:=\sqrt{d_\pm^2+\rho_\pm^2}.
\label{eq:eigs_final}
\end{equation}

Write
\begin{equation}
c_\pm=\rho_\pm e^{i\phi_\pm},
\qquad
\rho_\pm\ge 0,
\label{eq:cphase_final}
\end{equation}
and define the polar angle by
\begin{equation}
\cos\theta_\pm=\frac{d_\pm}{R_\pm},
\qquad
\sin\theta_\pm=\frac{\rho_\pm}{R_\pm}.
\label{eq:theta_final}
\end{equation}

A convenient normalized low eigenvector is
\begin{equation}
\eta_\pm
=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\,e^{-i\phi_\pm}\sin(\theta_\pm/2)\\
\cos(\theta_\pm/2)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:eta_angle_final}
\end{equation}
up to an irrelevant overall phase.

Equivalently, in algebraic ratio form, define
\begin{equation}
r_\pm
:=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{d_\pm+R_\pm},
\label{eq:rpm_final}
\end{equation}
whenever \(d_\pm+R_\pm\neq 0\), and then
\begin{equation}
\eta_\pm
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{1+|r_\pm|^2}}
\begin{pmatrix}
1\\
r_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:eta_ratio_final}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact formula for \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-
=
\overline{A_1^{(+)}}A_1^{(-)}
-
\overline{A_2^{(+)}}A_2^{(-)},
\label{eq:Delta_def_final}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\eta_\pm=
\begin{pmatrix}
A_1^{(\pm)}\\
A_2^{(\pm)}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Using \eqref{eq:eta_angle_final}, one gets
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{00}
=
e^{i(\phi_+-\phi_-)}
\sin\frac{\theta_+}{2}\sin\frac{\theta_-}{2}
-
\cos\frac{\theta_+}{2}\cos\frac{\theta_-}{2}.
\label{eq:Delta_angle_final}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:eta_ratio_final}, one obtains the fully algebraic expression
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_ratio_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact vanishing condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\label{eq:Delta_zero_final}
\end{equation}

Hence \(\Delta_{00}\) is nonzero generically.
Its vanishing requires a tuned matching relation between the two low-valley eigenvectors.

\section{4. Exact formula for \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel}}

Define the shell-normal intervalley \(J\)-matrix
\begin{equation}
U_\parallel
:=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Uparallel_final}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\label{eq:uparallel_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if
\begin{equation}
U_\parallel
=
u_0\mathbf 1_2+u_1\Sigma_1+u_2\Sigma_2+u_3\Sigma_3,
\label{eq:Uparallel_pauli_final}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel=u_3.
}
\label{eq:uparallel_u3_final}
\end{equation}

So the shell-normal longitudinal bias depends only on the \(\Sigma_3\)-component of the intervalley \(J\)-block.

\section{5. Exact formula for \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{L*}}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\label{eq:Lstar_def_final}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})
=
m_\parallel u_3.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_final}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_3=0.
}
\label{eq:Lstar_zero_final}
\end{equation}

So once \(m_\parallel\neq 0\), the only way the longitudinal slot dies is the exact diagonal cancellation
\[
u_{11}=u_{22}.
\]

\section{6. Practical sufficient condition for longitudinal survival}

In the current canonical branch, the longitudinal witness is controlled by the dominant product
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*},
\label{eq:dominant_product_final}
\end{equation}
up to the explicit remainder \(R_N\).
Therefore a practical sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:practical_suff_final2}
\end{equation}

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:ultramin_final2}
\end{equation}

Substituting the explicit formulas, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}
\right|
\cdot
|\alpha_X|
\cdot
\left|
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22})
\right|
\cdot
|A_{G_*}|
>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:fully_explicit_suff_final}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Reduced longitudinal coefficient in the current canonical branch}

The canonical witness formula gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_canonical_final}
\end{equation}
Thus, if \(\Delta_{00}\neq 0\), \(L_*\neq 0\), \(\alpha_X\neq 0\), and \(A_{G_*}\neq 0\), then the first-shell dominant compression yields
\[
m_3\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\section{8. Generic nonvanishing statement}

The two potential failure mechanisms are now explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\Delta_{00}=0\) only on the tuned locus
\[
\overline{r_+}r_-=1;
\]

\item \(L_*=0\) only if
\[
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore, absent an exact symmetry enforcing either condition, the longitudinal slot is generically nonzero once
\[
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
\]

\section{9. Honest status}

What is closed is the exact finite audit map
\[
(E_+(0),E_-(0),U_\parallel,m_\parallel)
\longmapsto
(\Delta_{00},L_*).
\]
What is still open is only the final microscopic insertion of the entries
\[
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel.
\]
So the remaining frontier is not structural.
It is a finite symbolic or numerical matrix-element computation.

\section{Final Summary}

The carrier-side longitudinal frontier is now reduced to the finite extraction of two scalars:
\[
\Delta_{00},
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

Write
\[
E_\pm(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & c_\pm\\
\overline{c_\pm} & b_\pm
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
U_\parallel=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then the normalized low eigenvectors of \(E_\pm(0)\) determine
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}},
\qquad
r_\pm=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=0
\iff
\overline{r_+}r_-=1.
}
\]

Next,
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
}
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
L_*=0
\iff
m_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
u_{11}=u_{22}.
}
\]

In the current canonical branch, the practical sufficient condition for longitudinal survival is
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\]
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore the longitudinal frontier is no longer structural.
It is reduced to the explicit microscopic insertion of the finite matrix entries
\[
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Shell-Harmonic Insertion Sheet for \texorpdfstring{$E_\pm(0)$}{Epm(0)}, \texorpdfstring{$U_\parallel$}{Uparallel}, and \texorpdfstring{$m_\parallel$}{mparallel} on the Locked 12-Mode BCC Background}

\section{Short explanation}

The remaining longitudinal audit is now a literal finite matrix-element computation.
Its exact finite audit map is
\[
(E_+(0),E_-(0),U_\parallel,m_\parallel)\longmapsto(\Delta_{00},L_*),
\]
with
\[
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
u_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel).
\]

Thus the correct next step is to write the actual matrix entries
\[
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel
\]
directly from the shell-harmonic Bloch operator of the locked 12-mode BCC background.

\section{1. Folded Bragg convention and locked 12-mode BCC background}

Fix the folded Bragg convention
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
}
\label{eq:BCC_folded_conv}
\end{equation}

Choose the first BCC reciprocal shell
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{12}
=
\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),\,
(\pm1,0,\pm1),\,
(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\},
\qquad
|\mathcal S_{12}|=12.
}
\label{eq:BCC_S12_explicit}
\end{equation}
The locked periodic background is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:BCC_locked_bg}
\end{equation}

Choose an internal basis adapted to the locked splitting
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_0=z_0,
\qquad
u_1,u_2\in Q_{z_0},
\qquad
u_r^\dagger u_s=\delta_{rs},
\qquad
\mathbb C^3=\mathbb Cz_0\oplus Q_{z_0}.
}
\label{eq:BCC_internal_basis}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Bloch-harmonic expansion of the microscopic fluctuations}

Expand the triplet fluctuation as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta\Psi_k(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G\in\Lambda^*}\sum_{r=0}^2
c_{G,r}\,u_r\,e^{iG\cdot x},
}
\label{eq:BCC_deltaPsi_Bloch}
\end{equation}
where \(\Lambda^*\) is the reciprocal lattice generated by the periodic BCC background.

The effective Bloch operator has the convolution form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
=
h^{\mathrm{diag}}_{rs}(k+G)\delta_{G,G'}
+
V^{\mathrm{eff}}_{rs}(G'-G;k+G),
}
\label{eq:BCC_Heff_general}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:BCC_Heff_Schur}
\end{equation}

Thus every matrix entry needed below is a finite matrix element of the actual refined locked Bloch operator.

\section{3. Shell-relevant doubled local block}

At the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\), define the local doubled shell basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|+,a\rangle:=|G=0,\ u_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|G=-G_*,\ u_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2.
}
\label{eq:BCC_shell_basis}
\end{equation}
Then the shell-relevant doubled space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D
=
\mathrm{span}\{|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle\}
\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\label{eq:BCC_HD}
\end{equation}

The shell block at \(p=0\) is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_D(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(0) & M(0)\\
M(0)^\dagger & E_-(0)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:BCC_HD_block}
\end{equation}
where \(E_\pm(0)\) are the \(2\times2\) valley-diagonal blocks and \(M(0)\) is the Bragg mixing block.

\section{4. Exact shell-harmonic formulas for \texorpdfstring{$E_\pm(0)$}{Epm(0)}}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0))_{ab}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad
(E_-(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*)|-,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:BCC_Epm_def}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:BCC_Heff_general} and \eqref{eq:BCC_shell_basis}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0))_{ab}
=
h^{\mathrm{diag}}_{ab}(k_*)
+
V^{\mathrm{eff}}_{ab}(0;k_*),
}
\label{eq:BCC_Eplus_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_-(0))_{ab}
=
h^{\mathrm{diag}}_{ab}(-k_*)
+
V^{\mathrm{eff}}_{ab}(0;-k_*).
}
\label{eq:BCC_Eminus_explicit}
\end{equation}

Therefore the finite matrix entries are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_+=(E_+(0))_{11},
\qquad
b_+=(E_+(0))_{22},
\qquad
c_+=(E_+(0))_{12},
}
\label{eq:BCC_aplus_bplus_cplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_-=(E_-(0))_{11},
\qquad
b_-=(E_-(0))_{22},
\qquad
c_-=(E_-(0))_{12}.
}
\label{eq:BCC_aminus_bminus_cminus}
\end{equation}

So once the refined locked core \(h^{\mathrm{diag}}\) and the Schur-corrected periodic coefficient \(V^{\mathrm{eff}}\) are fixed,
the valley matrices \(E_\pm(0)\) are explicit finite \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrices.

\section{5. Bragg mixing block and the role of \texorpdfstring{$A_{G_*}$}{A_G*}}

The intervalley Bragg block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{ab}(0)=\langle +,a|H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*)|-,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:BCC_M0_def}
\end{equation}
Using the convolution rule,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{ab}(0)=V^{\mathrm{eff}}_{ab}(-G_*;k_*).
}
\label{eq:BCC_M0_conv}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, since the leading background harmonics satisfy \(Q\in\mathcal S_{12}\),
the first-shell dominant intervalley mixing is controlled by the single shell Fourier amplitude \(A_{G_*}\).

Thus the finite shell problem separates naturally into:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the valley-diagonal \(2\times2\) Hermitian blocks \(E_\pm(0)\);
\item the intervalley shell amplitude \(A_{G_*}\) through \(M(0)\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{6. Low valley eigenvectors and \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

Let
\begin{equation}
E_\pm(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_\pm & c_\pm\\
\overline{c_\pm} & b_\pm
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:BCC_Epm_matrix}
\end{equation}
Diagonalize \(E_\pm(0)\) and let \(\eta_\pm\) be the normalized low eigenvectors.
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-.
}
\label{eq:BCC_Delta00_eta}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_\pm
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}},
}
\label{eq:BCC_rpm}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline r_+r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\label{eq:BCC_Delta00_ratio}
\end{equation}

So \(\Delta_{00}\) is already an explicit rational function of the six finite entries
\[
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm.
\]

\section{7. Exact shell-harmonic formula for \texorpdfstring{$U_\parallel$}{Uparallel}}

Define the shell-relevant reduced \(J\)-matrix by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\Bigl(\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)\Bigr)_{a,b=1}^2,
\qquad
\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)
=
\langle -,a|\mathsf J_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:BCC_Uj_def}
\end{equation}
Then the shell-normal reduced matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel
:=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:BCC_Uparallel_def}
\end{equation}

By direct shell-harmonic insertion,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{ab}
=
\hat n^j
\sum_{G,G'\in\Lambda^*}
\overline{c_{a,G}^{(-)}}
\,
\mathsf J_{j}^{\mathrm{eff}}(G'-G;\,k_*+G)
\,
c_{b,G'}^{(+)}.
}
\label{eq:BCC_uab_exact_sum}
\end{equation}
This is the exact finite-harmonic matrix element formula.
In the first-shell dominant truncation, only the leading intervalley harmonic survives, so operationally
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{ab}
\approx
\langle -,a|\hat n^j\mathsf J_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:BCC_uab_firstshell}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Canonical shell form of the \(J\)-kernel and extraction of \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel}}

In the canonical locked basis, the shell-relevant \(J\)-harmonic coefficient has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3}\,i(G_*)_i A_{G_*}
\Big[
u_\parallel\,\hat n_j\Sigma_3
+
u_E\,(e_{1j}\Sigma_1+e_{2j}\Sigma_2)
+
u_O\,(-e_{2j}\Sigma_1+e_{1j}\Sigma_2)
\Big]_r{}^{b}.
}
\label{eq:BCC_Jcanonical}
\end{equation}
Hence the shell-normal singlet coefficient is extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12\Bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:BCC_uparallel_extract}
\end{equation}

So the only longitudinally relevant part of the \(J\)-kernel is the diagonal shell-normal asymmetry of the reduced \(2\times2\) intervalley matrix.

\section{9. Exact formula for \texorpdfstring{$m_\parallel$}{m_parallel} and \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{L*}}

In the canonical locked frame, the background selector is aligned as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a(P_0)=m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3}.
}
\label{eq:BCC_malign}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:BCC_mparallel}
\end{equation}
No further reduction is needed.

Thus the final scalar invariant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:BCC_Lstar_final}
\end{equation}

\section{10. Direct longitudinal witness reconstruction}

The first-shell dominant pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal contribution is controlled by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak L_\parallel^{(JJ)}
=
\frac{|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|}{2}
\Bigl(
\Delta_{00}\,\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
+
R_N
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:BCC_Lmaster}
\end{equation}
and in the current canonical branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)
\propto
\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:BCC_VJJ_canonical}
\end{equation}
Therefore the practical sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\label{eq:BCC_practical_sufficient}
\end{equation}
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to require
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:BCC_ultramin}
\end{equation}

\section{11. Final reduced coefficient}

Once the primitive longitudinal slot survives, the reduced Branch-B coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3}
}
\label{eq:BCC_lambda_final}
\end{equation}
in the current canonical witness normalization.

Thus the complete longitudinal audit is now reduced to the explicit finite insertion of
\[
a_\pm,\quad b_\pm,\quad c_\pm,\quad
u_{11},\quad u_{22},\quad
m_\parallel,\quad
A_{G_*},\quad
R_N.
\]

\section{12. Honest status}

What is fully reduced is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-harmonic formulas for \(E_\pm(0)\);
\item the shell-harmonic formula for \(U_\parallel\);
\item the exact extraction formulas for \(\Delta_{00}\) and \(L_*\);
\item the practical sufficient condition \eqref{eq:BCC_practical_sufficient}.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is only the explicit symbolic or numerical insertion of the finite harmonic matrix elements for the final chosen refined locked microscopic operator.

\section{Final Summary}

On the locked 12-mode BCC background
\[
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger,
\]
the remaining longitudinal audit is a finite shell-harmonic matrix-element problem.

The valley-diagonal \(2\times2\) blocks are
\[
(E_+(0))_{ab}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad
(E_-(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*)|-,b\rangle,
\]
so
\[
a_\pm=(E_\pm(0))_{11},\qquad
b_\pm=(E_\pm(0))_{22},\qquad
c_\pm=(E_\pm(0))_{12}.
\]

Their low eigenvectors \(\eta_\pm\) determine
\[
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
\]
equivalently
\[
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline r_+r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}},
\qquad
r_\pm
=
-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}.
\]

The reduced shell-normal \(J\)-matrix is
\[
U_\parallel
=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\bigl(\langle -,a|\hat n^j\mathsf J_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle\bigr)_{a,b=1}^2,
\]
and the shell-normal singlet coefficient is
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12\bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\bigr].
\]

With
\[
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0),
\]
the final scalar invariant is
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\bigr].
\]

In the canonical first-shell dominant branch,
\[
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\propto \alpha_X L_* A_{G_*},
\]
so the practical sufficient condition is
\[
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
\]
In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough that
\[
\Delta_{00}\neq0,\qquad
L_*\neq0,\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
\]

Therefore the remaining longitudinal frontier is no longer structural.
It is the explicit finite insertion of the shell-harmonic data
\[
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel,\ A_{G_*},\ R_N.
\]
