\section{Direct Shell-Matrix Insertion of \texorpdfstring{$H_{\Psi\Psi}(k_*)$}{Hpsipsi(k*)}, \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal J(k_*)$}{J(k*)}, and \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal K(k_*)$}{K(k*)}}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present stage, the longitudinal audit is no longer a structural theorem problem.
It is the explicit shell-matrix insertion problem
\[
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k_*),\qquad \mathcal J(k_*),\qquad \mathcal K(k_*)
\Longrightarrow
E_\pm(0),\ M(0),\ U_\parallel,\ m_\parallel.
\]

The honest status is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(J\)-sector is explicit at the microscopic level;
\item the \(K\)-sector is only fixed in shell-relevant template form;
\item therefore the \(J\)-induced longitudinal block \(U_\parallel\) can already be written explicitly,
whereas the final \(K\)-dependent Schur-corrected entries remain partly parametric.
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Working branch and folded Bragg convention}

We work in the strongest explicit currently available microscopic branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\label{eq:insert_Lmic}
\end{equation}
We use the folded Bragg convention
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
}
\label{eq:insert_folded}
\end{equation}
The locked 12-mode BCC background is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:insert_locked_bg}
\end{equation}

Choose the canonical locked internal basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_0=z_0,
\qquad
u_1,u_2\in Q_{z_0},
\qquad
u_r^\dagger u_s=\delta_{rs},
\qquad
\mathbb C^3=\mathbb Cz_0\oplus Q_{z_0}.
}
\label{eq:insert_internal_basis}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Bloch-harmonic basis and shell carrier block}

Expand the triplet fluctuation in reciprocal harmonics:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta\Psi_k(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G\in\Lambda^*}\sum_{r=0}^2
c_{G,r}\,u_r\,e^{iG\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:insert_deltaPsi}
\end{equation}

Fix the shell carrier basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|+,a\rangle:=|G=0,u_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|G=-G_*,u_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2.
}
\label{eq:insert_shell_basis}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D
=
\mathrm{span}\{|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle\}
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\label{eq:insert_HD}
\end{equation}

The shell-restricted effective operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_D(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(0) & M(0)\\
M(0)^\dagger & E_-(0)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:insert_HD0}
\end{equation}
with \(2\times2\) internal blocks \(E_\pm(0)\) and intervalley Bragg block \(M(0)\).

\section{3. Exact Schur-corrected shell entries}

The effective triplet Bloch operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\mathcal C(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\mathcal C(k)^\dagger,
\qquad
\mathcal C(k):=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
}
\label{eq:insert_Heff_exact}
\end{equation}
At leading heavy-mass order,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal C(k)\mathcal C(k)^\dagger
+
O(M_X^{-4}).
}
\label{eq:insert_Heff_heavy}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact shell entries are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0))_{ab}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\Psi\Psi}(k_*)|+,b\rangle
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\langle \mathcal C_+^{(b)},\mathcal C_+^{(a)}\rangle_X
+
O(M_X^{-4}),
}
\label{eq:insert_Eplus_general}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_-(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|H_{\Psi\Psi}(k_*)|-,b\rangle
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\langle \mathcal C_-^{(b)},\mathcal C_-^{(a)}\rangle_X
+
O(M_X^{-4}),
}
\label{eq:insert_Eminus_general}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal C_\pm^{(a)}:=\mathcal C(k_*)|\pm,a\rangle,
\]
and \(\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_X\) is the internal mediator-fiber inner product.

Thus the six finite Hermitian valley entries are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_+=(E_+(0))_{11},
\qquad
b_+=(E_+(0))_{22},
\qquad
c_+=(E_+(0))_{12},
}
\label{eq:insert_aplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_-=(E_-(0))_{11},
\qquad
b_-=(E_-(0))_{22},
\qquad
c_-=(E_-(0))_{12}.
}
\label{eq:insert_aminus}
\end{equation}

Similarly, the intervalley Bragg block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{ab}(0)
=
\langle +,a|H_{\Psi\Psi}(k_*)|-,b\rangle
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\langle \mathcal C_-^{(b)},\mathcal C_+^{(a)}\rangle_X
+
O(M_X^{-4}).
}
\label{eq:insert_M_general}
\end{equation}

\section{4. What can be written explicitly for \texorpdfstring{$H_{\Psi\Psi}$}{Hpsipsi}}

Because the background is periodic, \(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\) has reciprocal-convolution form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
=
h^{\Psi\Psi}_{rs}(k+G)\delta_{G,G'}
+
V^{\Psi\Psi}_{rs}(G'-G;k).
}
\label{eq:insert_Hpsipsi_conv}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+(0))_{ab}^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
h^{\Psi\Psi}_{ab}(k_*)
+
V^{\Psi\Psi}_{ab}(0;k_*),
}
\label{eq:insert_Eplus_psipsi}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_-(0))_{ab}^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
h^{\Psi\Psi}_{ab}(-k_*)
+
V^{\Psi\Psi}_{ab}(0;-k_*),
}
\label{eq:insert_Eminus_psipsi}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{ab}^{(\Psi\Psi)}(0)=V^{\Psi\Psi}_{ab}(-G_*;k_*).
}
\label{eq:insert_M_psipsi}
\end{equation}

At the level of the locked Brazovskii core,
the diagonal symbol contains at least the scalar shell-forming piece.
The exact refined internal matrix part is encoded in \(h^{\Psi\Psi}_{ab}\) and remains dependent on the specific choice of \(L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}\).
Therefore the insertion formulas \eqref{eq:insert_Eplus_psipsi}--\eqref{eq:insert_M_psipsi} are exact,
but not yet numerically closed until \(L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}\) is fixed completely.

\section{5. Explicit linearization of \texorpdfstring{$J_i^a[\Psi]$}{J_i^a[Psi]}}

The microscopic current is explicitly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi).
}
\label{eq:insert_J_def}
\end{equation}
Linearizing around \(\Psi_0\),
\begin{equation}
\delta J_i^a
=
(\partial_i\delta\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi_0
+
(\partial_i\Psi_0^\dagger)T^a\delta\Psi
+
\delta\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi_0)
+
\Psi_0^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\delta\Psi).
\label{eq:insert_dJ_linear}
\end{equation}

Using
\[
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}A_Qe^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\delta\Psi_k(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G,r}c_{G,r}u_r e^{iG\cdot x},
\]
one gets the reciprocal-harmonic expansion
\begin{equation}
\delta J_i^a(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G,r}\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
c_{G,r}\,
e^{i(G+Q)\cdot x}\,
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)
+\mathrm{h.c.},
\label{eq:insert_dJ_harmonic}
\end{equation}
with explicit coefficient
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(Q;q)
=
i\,q_i\,A_Q\,u_r^\dagger T^a z_0
+
i\,Q_i\,A_Q\,z_0^\dagger T^a u_r,
\qquad q:=k+G.
}
\label{eq:insert_J_coeff}
\end{equation}

Thus the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic needed for the shell-pair intervalley channel is already explicit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;q)
=
i\,q_i\,A_{G_*}\,u_r^\dagger T^a z_0
+
i\,(G_*)_i\,A_{G_*}\,z_0^\dagger T^a u_r.
}
\label{eq:insert_J_Gstar}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Reduced \(J\)-matrix and extraction of \texorpdfstring{$U_\parallel$}{Uparallel}}

Define the reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:insert_Uj_def}
\end{equation}
Then the shell-normal reduced matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel:=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11}&u_{12}\\
u_{21}&u_{22}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:insert_Uparallel_def}
\end{equation}

Its exact finite-harmonic matrix-element form is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{ab}
=
\hat n^j
\sum_{G,G'\in\Lambda^*}
\overline{c_{a,G}^{(-)}}
\,
\mathsf J_{j}^{\mathrm{eff}}(G'-G;k_*+G)
\,
c_{b,G'}^{(+)}.
}
\label{eq:insert_uab_sum}
\end{equation}
In the first-shell dominant truncation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{ab}
\approx
\langle -,a|\hat n^j\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:insert_uab_1shell}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
}
\label{eq:insert_uparallel}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}),
\qquad
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:insert_Lstar}
\end{equation}

\section{7. What remains only template-level for \texorpdfstring{$K_i^a$}{K_i^a}}

The current notes fix only the shell-relevant template
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T^a\partial_iP)\,
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j{}^b+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j{}^b
\Bigr)
D_j\psi_b.
}
\label{eq:insert_K_template}
\end{equation}
On the defect background,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\,
\Bigl(
\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j{}^b+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j{}^b
\Bigr)
D_j\psi_b.
}
\label{eq:insert_K_defect}
\end{equation}

Therefore the \(K\)-sector is sufficient to parameterize the transverse \(E/O\) channels,
but it is not yet specified enough to give a fully explicit microscopic numerical matrix for
the \(K\)-dependent Schur correction in \eqref{eq:insert_Eplus_general}--\eqref{eq:insert_M_general}.

So the honest current split is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(J\)-sector and \(U_\parallel\): explicit;
\item \(K\)-sector: shell-template explicit, but not yet fully microscopic numeric.
\end{enumerate}

\section{8. Final executable insertion formulas}

The actual remaining finite entries are therefore computed by the following chain:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm
\ \text{from}\
\eqref{eq:insert_Eplus_general},\eqref{eq:insert_Eminus_general},
}
\label{eq:insert_exec1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_{11},u_{22}
\ \text{from}\
\eqref{eq:insert_uab_sum}
\ \text{or}\ 
\eqref{eq:insert_uab_1shell},
}
\label{eq:insert_exec2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline r_+r_-}{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}},
\qquad
r_\pm=-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}},
}
\label{eq:insert_exec3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}),
}
\label{eq:insert_exec4}
\end{equation}
and finally
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
}
\label{eq:insert_exec5}
\end{equation}
in the first-shell dominant canonical branch.

\section{9. Honest status}

What is already explicit:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell basis;
\item the Schur-corrected shell-entry formulas;
\item the microscopic \(J\)-current and its \(Q=G_*\) harmonic coefficient;
\item the reduced \(J\)-matrix \(U_\parallel\) and the scalar \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\).
\end{enumerate}

What is not yet fully explicit:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the complete refined internal symbol inside \(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\), because \(L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}\) is not yet fixed uniquely;
\item the full microscopic \(K\)-matrix beyond its shell-relevant template form.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the remaining frontier is no longer structural.
It is the explicit insertion of the final chosen refined locked microscopic constitutive data into the finite formulas above.

\section{Final Summary}

The remaining longitudinal shell audit is now an explicit finite matrix-element insertion problem.

The shell carrier basis is
\[
|+,a\rangle:=|G=0,u_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|G=-G_*,u_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2,
\]
and the shell-restricted block is
\[
H_D(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(0) & M(0)\\
M(0)^\dagger & E_-(0)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Its exact Schur-corrected entries are
\[
(E_\pm(0))_{ab}
=
\langle \pm,a|H_{\Psi\Psi}(k_*)|\pm,b\rangle
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\langle \mathcal C_\pm^{(b)},\mathcal C_\pm^{(a)}\rangle_X
+
O(M_X^{-4}),
\]
with
\[
\mathcal C(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\]

The \(J\)-sector is already explicit:
\[
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi),
\]
so after linearization around
\[
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x},
\]
the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic coefficient is
\[
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;q)
=
i\,q_i\,A_{G_*}\,u_r^\dagger T^a z_0
+
i\,(G_*)_i\,A_{G_*}\,z_0^\dagger T^a u_r.
\]

Therefore the reduced intervalley shell-normal \(J\)-matrix
\[
U_\parallel=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),
\qquad
\mathcal U_{j,ab}(0)=\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle,
\]
is explicit, and
\[
u_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)=\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
\]

By contrast, the \(K\)-sector is currently fixed only at shell-template level:
\[
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T^a\partial_iP)\,
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j{}^b+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j{}^b\bigr)D_j\psi_b,
\]
so the full \(K\)-dependent Schur correction is not yet microscopically numerically closed.

Hence the exact present status is:

\[
\boxed{
J\text{-sector and }U_\parallel\text{: explicit,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
K\text{-sector: template explicit only,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
a_\pm,b_\pm,c_\pm,u_{11},u_{22}
\text{ are now reduced to a finite constitutive-data insertion problem.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Core-Only Explicit Shell Matrix for \texorpdfstring{$H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)$}{Hpsipsi(k)} on the Locked 12-Mode BCC Background}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present stage, the cleanest nonredundant move is to separate the full shell matrix into:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \emph{core/refined triplet block} \(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\), which can already be written explicitly up to the still-unspecified refined internal terms;
\item the \emph{Class II Schur correction}, whose \(J\)-sector is explicit but whose full \(K\)-sector remains only template-level.
\end{enumerate}

This immediately yields an important partial result:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the pure locked Brazovskii core contributes an internal scalar shell block,}
}
\]
so any nontrivial \(\Sigma_3\)-resolved longitudinal carrier data must come from refined internal structure and/or the mediated \(J\)-sector.

\section{1. Locked 12-mode BCC background and shell basis}

Fix the equal-amplitude locked background
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger,
}
\label{eq:core_bg}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{12}
=
\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),(\pm1,0,\pm1),(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\},
\qquad
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
}
\label{eq:core_S12}
\end{equation}

Choose the locked internal basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_0=z_0,
\qquad
u_1,u_2\in Q_{z_0},
\qquad
u_r^\dagger u_s=\delta_{rs}.
}
\label{eq:core_intbasis}
\end{equation}

The shell carrier basis is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|+,a\rangle:=|G=0,u_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle:=|G=-G_*,u_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2.
}
\label{eq:core_shellbasis}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Core condensate operator in the tangent sector}

The core/refined condensate Lagrangian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}
=
|\partial_t\Psi|^2
-\mu^2\Psi^\dagger\Psi
+Z\,\partial_i\Psi^\dagger\partial_i\Psi
-Y\,(\nabla^2\Psi)^\dagger(\nabla^2\Psi)
-u(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)^2
+\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}.
}
\label{eq:core_Lcore}
\end{equation}

Linearize around
\[
\Psi_0=z_0\phi_0
\]
using tangent fluctuations
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta\Psi_k(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G\in\Lambda^*}\sum_{a=1}^2
c_{G,a}\,u_a\,e^{iG\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:core_deltapsi}
\end{equation}

Because \(u_a^\dagger z_0=0\), the quartic density term contributes only a scalar periodic density potential in the tangent sector. Therefore the tangent-sector Bloch operator has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}(k)\bigr)_{(G,a),(G',b)}
=
\delta_{ab}
\Bigl[
\omega_B(k+G)\delta_{G,G'}
+
2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(G'-G)
\Bigr]
+
R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(G'-G;k),
}
\label{eq:core_Hpsipsi_general}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega_B(q):=-\mu^2+Z|q|^2-Y|q|^4,
}
\label{eq:core_omegaB}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_0(x):=|\phi_0(x)|^2,
\qquad
\widehat{\rho_0}(Q)
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;e^{-iQ\cdot x}\rho_0(x).
}
\label{eq:core_rhohat}
\end{equation}
The matrix \(R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(Q;k)\) collects all still-unspecified refined internal derivative terms coming from \(\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}\).

\section{3. Explicit Fourier coefficients of the locked BCC density}

From
\[
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_0(x)=|\phi_0(x)|^2
=
A^2\sum_{Q,Q'\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{i(Q-Q')\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:core_rho0_expand}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho_0}(0)=12\,A^2\,|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|,
}
\label{eq:core_rho0_zero}
\end{equation}
and for the selected Bragg vector \(G_*\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\rho_0}(G_*)
=
N_{G_*}\,A^2\,|\Omega_{\mathrm{cell}}|,
}
\label{eq:core_rho0_Gstar}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N_{G_*}
:=
\#\left\{(Q,Q')\in\mathcal S_{12}^2:\ Q-Q'=G_*\right\}.
}
\label{eq:core_NGstar}
\end{equation}

So the core Bragg amplitude is an explicit finite shell-combinatorial quantity.

\section{4. Exact core formulas for \texorpdfstring{$E_\pm(0)$}{Epm(0)} and \texorpdfstring{$M(0)$}{M(0)}}

By restriction to the shell basis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+^{\mathrm{core}}(0))_{ab}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}(k_*)|+,b\rangle,
}
\label{eq:core_Eplus_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_-^{\mathrm{core}}(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}(k_*)|-,b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:core_Eminus_def}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:core_Hpsipsi_general},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+^{\mathrm{core}}(0))_{ab}
=
\delta_{ab}
\Bigl[
\omega_B(k_*)
+
2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(0)
\Bigr]
+
R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(0;k_*),
}
\label{eq:core_Eplus_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_-^{\mathrm{core}}(0))_{ab}
=
\delta_{ab}
\Bigl[
\omega_B(-k_*)
+
2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(0)
\Bigr]
+
R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(0;-k_*).
}
\label{eq:core_Eminus_explicit}
\end{equation}

Similarly, the core intervalley Bragg block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{ab}^{\mathrm{core}}(0)
=
\langle +,a|H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}(k_*)|-,b\rangle
=
\delta_{ab}\,2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(G_*)
+
R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(-G_*;k_*).
}
\label{eq:core_M_explicit}
\end{equation}

Therefore the finite valley entries are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_+^{\mathrm{core}}
=
\omega_B(k_*)+2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(0)+R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{11}(0;k_*),
\qquad
b_+^{\mathrm{core}}
=
\omega_B(k_*)+2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(0)+R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{22}(0;k_*),
}
\label{eq:core_aplus_bplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_+^{\mathrm{core}}=R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{12}(0;k_*),
}
\label{eq:core_cplus}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_-^{\mathrm{core}}
=
\omega_B(-k_*)+2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(0)+R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{11}(0;-k_*),
\qquad
b_-^{\mathrm{core}}
=
\omega_B(-k_*)+2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(0)+R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{22}(0;-k_*),
}
\label{eq:core_aminus_bminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_-^{\mathrm{core}}=R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{12}(0;-k_*).
}
\label{eq:core_cminus}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Important immediate consequence}

If the refined internal terms are absent or internally scalar in the locked basis, i.e.
\[
R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(Q;k)=r^{\mathrm{ref}}(Q;k)\,\delta_{ab},
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_+^{\mathrm{core}}=b_+^{\mathrm{core}},
\qquad
a_-^{\mathrm{core}}=b_-^{\mathrm{core}},
\qquad
c_+^{\mathrm{core}}=c_-^{\mathrm{core}}=0.
}
\label{eq:core_scalar_only}
\end{equation}

Thus the pure locked Brazovskii core produces an internal identity block on the tangent doublet:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm^{\mathrm{core}}(0)\propto \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M^{\mathrm{core}}(0)\propto \mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:core_identity_block}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the dangerous scalar Bragg route:
it produces the constant scalar Bragg block but no internal \(\Sigma_3\)-resolved longitudinal selector.

Therefore any genuinely nontrivial longitudinal \(2+2\) carrier data must come from:
\begin{enumerate}
\item refined non-scalar internal structure inside \(\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}\), and/or
\item the Class II mediated \(J\)-sector.
\end{enumerate}

\section{6. Explicit \(J\)-sector harmonic input for \texorpdfstring{$U_\parallel$}{Uparallel}}

The microscopic current is explicitly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi).
}
\label{eq:core_J_explicit}
\end{equation}
Linearizing around \(\Psi_0=z_0\phi_0\), one obtains the shell-relevant harmonic coefficient
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;q)
=
i\,q_i\,A_{G_*}\,u_r^\dagger T^a z_0
+
i\,(G_*)_i\,A_{G_*}\,z_0^\dagger T^a u_r.
}
\label{eq:core_J_Gstar}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced intervalley \(J\)-matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad
U_\parallel:=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0).
}
\label{eq:core_Uparallel_def}
\end{equation}
Its shell-normal \(\Sigma_3\)-component is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12\Bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:core_uparallel}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Bigr],
\qquad
m_\parallel=m^3(P_0).
}
\label{eq:core_Lstar}
\end{equation}

So \(U_\parallel\) is already explicit once the canonical locked internal basis \((z_0,u_1,u_2)\) and the chosen generator \(T^a\) are fixed.

\section{7. Honest split of what is explicit and what is still parametric}

At the present stage, the following are already explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell basis \(|\pm,a\rangle\);
\item the core shell matrix formulas \eqref{eq:core_Eplus_explicit}--\eqref{eq:core_M_explicit};
\item the density Fourier coefficients \(\widehat{\rho_0}(0)\) and \(\widehat{\rho_0}(G_*)\);
\item the microscopic \(J\)-current and its \(Q=G_*\) harmonic coefficient \eqref{eq:core_J_Gstar};
\item the reduced \(J\)-matrix \(U_\parallel\) and \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\).
\end{enumerate}

What is still parametric:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the non-scalar refined internal block \(R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(Q;k)\), because \(\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}\) has not yet been fixed uniquely;
\item the full microscopic \(K\)-matrix beyond its shell-template form.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the remaining frontier is not structural.
It is the insertion of the final constitutive data into the already explicit finite shell formulas.

\section{Final Summary}

For the locked 12-mode BCC background, the tangent-sector core Bloch operator is

\[
\bigl(H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}(k)\bigr)_{(G,a),(G',b)}
=
\delta_{ab}
\Bigl[
\omega_B(k+G)\delta_{G,G'}
+
2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(G'-G)
\Bigr]
+
R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(G'-G;k),
\]
with
\[
\omega_B(q)=-\mu^2+Z|q|^2-Y|q|^4,
\qquad
\rho_0(x)=|\phi_0(x)|^2.
\]

Therefore the shell entries are

\[
(E_+^{\mathrm{core}}(0))_{ab}
=
\delta_{ab}
\Bigl[
\omega_B(k_*)
+
2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(0)
\Bigr]
+
R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(0;k_*),
\]

\[
(E_-^{\mathrm{core}}(0))_{ab}
=
\delta_{ab}
\Bigl[
\omega_B(-k_*)
+
2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(0)
\Bigr]
+
R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(0;-k_*),
\]

\[
M_{ab}^{\mathrm{core}}(0)
=
\delta_{ab}\,2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(G_*)
+
R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(-G_*;k_*).
\]

If the refined internal terms are absent or internally scalar in the locked basis, then
\[
E_\pm^{\mathrm{core}}(0)\propto \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M^{\mathrm{core}}(0)\propto \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Hence the pure locked Brazovskii core reproduces the dangerous scalar Bragg block but does not produce a nontrivial \(\Sigma_3\)-resolved longitudinal selector.

The microscopic \(J\)-sector is already explicit:
\[
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi),
\]
and its shell-relevant harmonic coefficient is
\[
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;q)
=
i\,q_i\,A_{G_*}\,u_r^\dagger T^a z_0
+
i\,(G_*)_i\,A_{G_*}\,z_0^\dagger T^a u_r.
\]

Therefore the reduced intervalley shell-normal matrix
\[
U_\parallel=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),
\qquad
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{ab}=\langle -,a|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,b\rangle,
\]
is explicit, and
\[
u_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel),
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
\]

So the exact present verdict is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{core shell matrix: explicit up to }R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
J\text{-sector longitudinal selector: explicit,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
K\text{-sector full microscopic closure: still template-level.}
}
\]

Thus the remaining frontier is only the insertion of the final constitutive data into an already explicit finite shell matrix problem.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Evaluation of \texorpdfstring{$R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}$}{Rrefab} for the Minimal Safe Refined Alignment Term}

\section{Short explanation}

The previous core-only shell matrix formulas contained the still-unspecified refined internal block
\[
R^{\mathrm{ref}}_{ab}(Q;k).
\]
To avoid leaving this completely abstract, we now choose the only refined term that is both
explicitly available in the current notes and rigorously safe on the locked sector:
the projector-stiffness/alignment term
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{align}}
=
\frac{\chi}{4}\int d^3x\,
\rho^2\,\Tr(\partial_iP\,\partial_iP).
}
\label{eq:align_term_explicit}
\end{equation}

We show that this term gives
\[
R^{\mathrm{ref,align}}_{ab}(0;\pm k_*)=0,
\qquad
R^{\mathrm{ref,align}}_{ab}(-G_*;k_*)=0
\]
at tree level on the locked constant-projector background.
Its effect appears only indirectly after integrating out the heavy projector tangent mode.

\section{1. Locked background and fluctuation split}

Write
\[
\Psi=\rho z,
\qquad
P=zz^\dagger,
\qquad
z^\dagger z=1.
\]
On the locked 12-mode BCC background,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger,
\qquad
\partial_iP_0=0.
}
\label{eq:align_locked_bg}
\end{equation}

Introduce tangent fluctuations of the projector by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z=z_0+\eta-\frac12(\eta^\dagger\eta)z_0+\cdots,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger\eta=0,
\qquad
\eta\in Q_{z_0}.
}
\label{eq:align_eta_param}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta P
=
\eta z_0^\dagger+z_0\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
\partial_i\delta P
=
(\partial_i\eta)z_0^\dagger+z_0(\partial_i\eta^\dagger).
}
\label{eq:align_deltaP}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact vanishing on the locked sector}

Because \(P_0\) is constant,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{align}}[\Psi_0,P_0]=0.
}
\label{eq:align_zero_bg}
\end{equation}
Therefore this term does not modify:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell radius \(q_*\);
\item the scalar locked BCC selection at the background level;
\item the background shell Fourier amplitudes at tree level.
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, in the shell-matrix language, it contributes no background constant
Bragg block at zeroth order.

\section{3. Quadratic expansion of the alignment term}

Expand \eqref{eq:align_term_explicit} around \eqref{eq:align_locked_bg}.
Since \(\partial_iP_0=0\), the first nonzero term is quadratic:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{align}}^{(2)}
=
\frac{\chi}{4}\int d^3x\,
\bar\rho^2\,
\Tr(\partial_i\delta P\,\partial_i\delta P)
+
O(\delta\rho\,\eta^2,\eta^3),
}
\label{eq:align_quad0}
\end{equation}
where \(\bar\rho:=|\phi_0|\) on the locked background.

Using \eqref{eq:align_deltaP},
\begin{align}
\Tr(\partial_i\delta P\,\partial_i\delta P)
&=
\Tr\Bigl[
(\partial_i\eta)z_0^\dagger+z_0(\partial_i\eta^\dagger)
\Bigr]
\Bigl[
(\partial_i\eta)z_0^\dagger+z_0(\partial_i\eta^\dagger)
\Bigr]
\nonumber\\
&=
2\,(\partial_i\eta^\dagger)(\partial_i\eta),
\label{eq:align_trace_eval}
\end{align}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{align}}^{(2)}
=
\frac{\chi}{2}\int d^3x\,\bar\rho^2\,
(\partial_i\eta^\dagger)(\partial_i\eta).
}
\label{eq:align_quad_final}
\end{equation}

Thus the alignment term contributes a positive quadratic projector-tangent operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\eta\eta}^{\mathrm{align}}
=
\chi\,\bar\rho^2\,(-\nabla^2)
}
\label{eq:align_heavy_operator}
\end{equation}
on the heavy projector mode.

\section{4. Tree-level shell-matrix contribution to the tangent triplet block}

Now compare \eqref{eq:align_quad_final} with the tangent triplet shell block
\[
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k).
\]
The key point is that \(\mathcal F_{\mathrm{align}}^{(2)}\) is quadratic in the projector tangent mode \(\eta\),
not in the shell-carrying tangent triplet coefficients \(c_{G,a}\) directly.

Therefore, in the shell basis
\[
|+,a\rangle,\qquad |-,a\rangle,\qquad a=1,2,
\]
the direct tree-level contribution of the alignment term to the triplet shell block vanishes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{\mathrm{ref,align}}_{ab}(Q;k)=0
\qquad
\text{at tree level on the locked constant-projector background.}
}
\label{eq:Ralign_tree_zero_general}
\end{equation}

In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{\mathrm{ref,align}}_{ab}(0;k_*)=0,
\qquad
R^{\mathrm{ref,align}}_{ab}(0;-k_*)=0,
\qquad
R^{\mathrm{ref,align}}_{ab}(-G_*;k_*)=0.
}
\label{eq:Ralign_tree_zero_specific}
\end{equation}

Hence the core shell entries remain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_+^{\mathrm{core+align,tree}}(0))_{ab}
=
\delta_{ab}
\Bigl[
\omega_B(k_*)
+
2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(0)
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:Eplus_core_align_tree}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(E_-^{\mathrm{core+align,tree}}(0))_{ab}
=
\delta_{ab}
\Bigl[
\omega_B(-k_*)
+
2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(0)
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:Eminus_core_align_tree}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{ab}^{\mathrm{core+align,tree}}(0)
=
\delta_{ab}\,2u\,\widehat{\rho_0}(G_*).
}
\label{eq:M_core_align_tree}
\end{equation}

So the direct shell block remains proportional to the internal identity:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E_\pm^{\mathrm{core+align,tree}}(0)\propto \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M^{\mathrm{core+align,tree}}(0)\propto \mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:core_align_identity}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Interpretation: no direct Branch-A seed from the explicit safe refined term}

Equation \eqref{eq:core_align_identity} implies immediately that the explicit safe refined term
\(\mathcal F_{\mathrm{align}}\) does \emph{not} generate a nontrivial internal
\(\Sigma_3\)-resolved valley selector at tree level.
Therefore it does not provide a direct constant-leading Branch-A coefficient:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\big|_{\mathrm{align,tree}}=0.
}
\label{eq:align_no_branchA}
\end{equation}

So the projector-stiffness refinement is structurally safe but not a direct longitudinal source.

\section{6. Induced effect after heavy-mode elimination}

Although the direct tree-level contribution vanishes,
\(\mathcal F_{\mathrm{align}}\) makes the projector tangent mode heavy.
Hence, if an admissible shell--projector mixing source
\[
\mathcal J_{\Psi\eta}
\]
exists, then integrating out \(\eta\) induces a second-order correction of Schur type:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\Psi\Psi}^{(\mathrm{align,ind})}
=
-
H_{\Psi\eta}\,
(H_{\eta\eta}^{\mathrm{align}})^{-1}
\,H_{\eta\Psi}.
}
\label{eq:align_induced_Schur}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:align_heavy_operator},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(H_{\eta\eta}^{\mathrm{align}})^{-1}
\sim
\frac{1}{\chi\,\bar\rho^2\,q_*^2}
}
\label{eq:align_inverse_scale}
\end{equation}
at shell scale.
Therefore the induced shell corrections satisfy the parametric bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta E_\pm^{(\mathrm{align,ind})},
\quad
\delta M^{(\mathrm{align,ind})},
\quad
\delta W_\parallel^{(\mathrm{align,ind})},
\quad
\delta W_I^{(\mathrm{align,ind})},
\quad
\delta W_J^{(\mathrm{align,ind})}
=
O\!\left(\frac{1}{\chi\bar\rho^2 q_*^2}\right),
}
\label{eq:align_induced_bound}
\end{equation}
provided the microscopic shell sector couples to the projector tangent mode with the admissible tensor structure.

\section{7. Honest endpoint}

Thus the explicit refined alignment term gives the following exact status:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it is zero on the locked background and preserves the scalar locked reduction;
\item it gives a positive heavy quadratic operator to the projector tangent mode;
\item it does not generate a direct tree-level shell-enriched tensor;
\item consequently
\[
R^{\mathrm{ref,align}}_{ab}(Q;k)=0
\quad
\text{for the shell triplet block at tree level};
\]
\item any effect on the actual witness coefficients arises only indirectly, after heavy-mode elimination,
and depends on the still-open explicit shell--projector mixing source.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the explicit safe refined term confirms, rather than changes, the current mainline:
the direct explicit longitudinal selector is still supplied by the Branch-B/Class-II route,
not by the tree-level projector stiffness term.

\section{Final Summary}

Choose the explicit safe refined term
\[
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{align}}
=
\frac{\chi}{4}\int d^3x\,\rho^2\,\Tr(\partial_iP\,\partial_iP).
\]

On the locked 12-mode BCC background
\[
\Psi_0=z_0\phi_0,
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger,
\qquad
\partial_iP_0=0,
\]
this term vanishes exactly at the background level:
\[
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{align}}[\Psi_0,P_0]=0.
\]

Its first nonzero contribution is quadratic in the projector tangent fluctuation \(\eta\):
\[
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{align}}^{(2)}
=
\frac{\chi}{2}\int d^3x\,\bar\rho^2\,
(\partial_i\eta^\dagger)(\partial_i\eta),
\]
so it defines the heavy projector operator
\[
H_{\eta\eta}^{\mathrm{align}}
=
\chi\,\bar\rho^2\,(-\nabla^2).
\]

Therefore it contributes no direct tree-level correction to the tangent-triplet shell block:
\[
\boxed{
R^{\mathrm{ref,align}}_{ab}(0;\pm k_*)=0,
\qquad
R^{\mathrm{ref,align}}_{ab}(-G_*;k_*)=0.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
E_\pm^{\mathrm{core+align,tree}}(0)\propto \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M^{\mathrm{core+align,tree}}(0)\propto \mathbf 1_2.
}
\]

So the explicit safe refined term does not generate a direct internal \(\Sigma_3\)-resolved selector and does not provide a tree-level Branch-A longitudinal seed:
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\big|_{\mathrm{align,tree}}=0.
}
\]

Its effect appears only indirectly after integrating out the heavy projector tangent mode:
\[
\delta H_{\Psi\Psi}^{(\mathrm{align,ind})}
=
-
H_{\Psi\eta}(H_{\eta\eta}^{\mathrm{align}})^{-1}H_{\eta\Psi},
\]
which yields induced shell corrections of order
\[
\boxed{
O\!\left(\frac{1}{\chi\bar\rho^2 q_*^2}\right),
}
\]
provided an admissible shell--projector mixing source exists.

Therefore the explicit safe refined term confirms the current mainline:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the direct explicit longitudinal selector is still the Branch-B/Class-II route,}
}
\]
not the tree-level projector-stiffness sector.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Direct Canonical Extraction of \texorpdfstring{$U_\parallel$}{Uparallel} and \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel}}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present stage, the carrier-side longitudinal frontier is no longer a tensor-classification problem.
It is the extraction of the single scalar
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)\bigr),
\]
in the canonical locked basis.

Once this scalar is known, the longitudinal invariant is
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\]
and in the minimal explicit canonical split,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

\section{1. Canonical locked basis}

Fix the canonical locked basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0=(1,0,0)^T,
\qquad
u_1=(0,1,0)^T,
\qquad
u_2=(0,0,1)^T.
}
\label{eq:Upar_can_basis}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
Q_{z_0}=\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb C}\{u_1,u_2\},
\]
and the tangent Pauli matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_1=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
1&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\Sigma_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-i\\
i&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\Sigma_3=
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0\\
0&-1
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Upar_Pauli}
\end{equation}

Fix also the shell frame
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\},
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
}
\label{eq:Upar_shell_frame}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Explicit microscopic \(J\)-criterion in this basis}

The \(J\)-block is explicitly known once \(z_0\) and \((u_1,u_2)\) are fixed, and the relevant tangent-shell couplings are controlled by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
t_{\alpha0}^a:=u_\alpha^\dagger T^a z_0,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Upar_ta0}
\end{equation}
In the canonical basis \eqref{eq:Upar_can_basis},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
t_{10}^a=(T^a)_{21},
\qquad
t_{20}^a=(T^a)_{31}.
}
\label{eq:Upar_ta0_entries}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact microscopic coupling criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J(k)\text{ couples the shell-tangent doublet to the mediator}
\iff
(T^a)_{21}\neq 0
\ \text{or}\ 
(T^a)_{31}\neq 0
\ \text{for some active }a.
}
\label{eq:Upar_coupling_criterion}
\end{equation}

So in the canonical locked basis, the \(J\)-sector coupling question is a literal finite internal-matrix test.

\section{3. Bragg-matched shell restriction}

At the folded Bragg point, the shell basis is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|+\!,\alpha\rangle\equiv|G=0,\alpha\rangle,
\qquad
|-\!,\alpha\rangle\equiv|G=-G_*,\alpha\rangle,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Upar_shell_pair_basis}
\end{equation}
The exact Bragg matching condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0=(-G_*)+Q
\iff
Q=G_*,
}
\label{eq:Upar_Bragg}
\end{equation}
so only the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic contributes directly to the intervalley shell block. 

Thus the reduced \(J\)-matrix is defined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mathcal U_j(0))_{\alpha\beta}
:=
\langle -,\alpha|\widehat{\mathsf J}_j(G_*;0)|+,\beta\rangle.
}
\label{eq:Upar_Uj_def}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Canonical decomposition of the \(J\)-sector tensor}

The shell-relevant \(J\)-tensor decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0)
=
u_\parallel\,\hat n_j\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{b}
+
u_E\,(e_{1j}\Sigma_1+e_{2j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
u_O\,(-e_{2j}\Sigma_1+e_{1j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
\mathcal U^{\mathrm{irr}}_{jr}{}^{b}.
}
\label{eq:Upar_Udecomp}
\end{equation}

Projecting along \(\hat n^j\), one gets
\begin{equation}
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
u_\parallel\Sigma_3
+
\hat n^j\mathcal U^{\mathrm{irr}}_j(0),
\label{eq:Upar_nproj_general}
\end{equation}
because
\[
\hat n\cdot e_1=\hat n\cdot e_2=0.
\]
Hence the exact projector formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr\!\Bigl(
\Sigma_3\,\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:Upar_trace_formula}
\end{equation}

If the irreducible remainder has no shell-normal \(\Sigma_3\)-singlet component in the chosen truncation,
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel:=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)=u_\parallel\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Upar_minimal_split_matrix}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Explicit matrix form of \texorpdfstring{$U_\parallel$}{Uparallel}}

Under the minimal explicit canonical split,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\parallel
=
u_\parallel
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0\\
0&-1
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Upar_explicit_matrix}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(U_\parallel)_{11}=u_\parallel,
\qquad
(U_\parallel)_{22}=-u_\parallel,
\qquad
(U_\parallel)_{12}=(U_\parallel)_{21}=0.
}
\label{eq:Upar_entries}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Upar_diag_diff}
\end{equation}

Thus the longitudinal shell-normal \(J\)-singlet survives if and only if the two carrier basis states are split in the \(\Sigma_3\) direction:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel\neq 0
\iff
(U_\parallel)_{11}\neq (U_\parallel)_{22}.
}
\label{eq:Upar_split_criterion}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Background selector and \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{L*}}

In the canonical locked reduction, the background selector aligns with the singlet axis:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a(P_0)=m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3}.
}
\label{eq:Upar_malign}
\end{equation}
Therefore the longitudinal invariant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:Upar_Lstar}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Upar_diag_diff},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Upar_Lstar_diag}
\end{equation}

So the actual remaining longitudinal scalar check is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
(U_\parallel)_{11}\neq (U_\parallel)_{22}.
}
\label{eq:Upar_scalar_check}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Reduced witness coefficient}

In the current canonical split, the reduced witness coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:Upar_lambda_final}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
u_\parallel\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:Upar_lambda_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Optional explicit internal-algebra check}

In the canonical basis, the shell-tangent couplings are the first-column off-diagonal entries
\[
t_{10}^a=(T^a)_{21},
\qquad
t_{20}^a=(T^a)_{31}.
\]
So the microscopic origin of a nonzero \(u_\parallel\) is an actual \(J\)-induced asymmetry between the two tangent channels \((u_1,u_2)\).

Therefore the last honest fork is exactly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{either verify an actual internal \(J\)-split between }u_1,u_2,
\quad\text{or compute }(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\text{ directly.}
}
\label{eq:Upar_last_fork}
\end{equation}

\section{9. Honest status}

What is fully closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the canonical locked basis;
\item the exact projector formula for \(u_\parallel\);
\item the identification
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel;
\]
\item the reduced witness formula
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\alpha_X m_\parallel u_\parallel I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is only the explicit microscopic value of \(u_\parallel\), equivalently the direct evaluation of
\[
(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}
\]
for the final chosen refined locked operator.

\section{Final Summary}

In the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=(1,0,0)^T,
\qquad
u_1=(0,1,0)^T,
\qquad
u_2=(0,0,1)^T,
\]
the shell-relevant \(J\)-tensor decomposes as
\[
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0)
=
u_\parallel\,\hat n_j\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{b}
+
u_E\,(e_{1j}\Sigma_1+e_{2j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
u_O\,(-e_{2j}\Sigma_1+e_{1j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
\mathcal U^{\mathrm{irr}}_{jr}{}^{b}.
\]

Therefore the shell-normal reduced matrix is
\[
U_\parallel:=\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0),
\]
and the longitudinal scalar is extracted by the exact projector formula
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\Sigma_3U_\parallel\bigr)
=
\frac12\Bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Bigr].
}
\]

Under the minimal explicit canonical split, one has
\[
U_\parallel=u_\parallel\Sigma_3,
\]
so explicitly
\[
\boxed{
(U_\parallel)_{11}=u_\parallel,
\qquad
(U_\parallel)_{22}=-u_\parallel.
}
\]

The background selector aligns as
\[
m^a(P_0)=m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3},
\]
hence the longitudinal invariant is
\[
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}
\Bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Bigr].
}
\]

In the current canonical reduced witness normalization,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]
So
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(U_\parallel)_{11}\neq(U_\parallel)_{22}
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\]

Finally, the microscopic \(J\)-coupling criterion is finite and explicit:
\[
t_{10}^a=(T^a)_{21},
\qquad
t_{20}^a=(T^a)_{31},
\]
so the shell-tangent doublet couples to the mediator iff some active generator has a nonzero first-column off-diagonal entry.

Therefore the longitudinal carrier frontier is no longer structural.
It is the explicit finite evaluation of the diagonal asymmetry
\[
(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual internal-generator calculation of the longitudinal \(J\)-split}

Fix the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=e_1=
\begin{pmatrix}
1\\0\\0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u_1=e_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\1\\0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u_2=e_3=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\0\\1
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Let the internal generators be the standard Hermitian \(SU(3)\) basis
\[
T^a=\frac{\lambda^a}{2}.
\]
Then the only entries relevant for the shell-tangent coupling are
\[
t_{10}^a:=u_1^\dagger T^a z_0=(T^a)_{21},
\qquad
t_{20}^a:=u_2^\dagger T^a z_0=(T^a)_{31}.
\]

For the standard Gell-Mann basis one gets explicitly
\[
T^1=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1&0\\
1&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
T^2=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-i&0\\
i&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
\[
T^3=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0&0\\
0&-1&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
T^4=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&1\\
0&0&0\\
1&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
\[
T^5=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&-i\\
0&0&0\\
i&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
T^6=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&0\\
0&0&1\\
0&1&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
\[
T^7=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&0\\
0&0&-i\\
0&i&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
T^8=\frac{1}{2\sqrt3}
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0&0\\
0&1&0\\
0&0&-2
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Therefore
\[
(t_{10}^a,t_{20}^a)=
\begin{cases}
\left(\frac12,0\right), & a=1,\\[1mm]
\left(\frac{i}{2},0\right), & a=2,\\[1mm]
(0,0), & a=3,\\[1mm]
\left(0,\frac12\right), & a=4,\\[1mm]
\left(0,\frac{i}{2}\right), & a=5,\\[1mm]
(0,0), & a=6,7,8.
\end{cases}
\]

So only the four generators
\[
T^1,\ T^2,\ T^4,\ T^5
\]
couple the locked direction \(z_0\) to the tangent doublet \((u_1,u_2)\).
Moreover,

\[
T^{1,2}:\ z_0\leftrightarrow u_1,
\qquad
T^{4,5}:\ z_0\leftrightarrow u_2,
\]
while
\[
T^3,\ T^6,\ T^7,\ T^8
\]
do \emph{not} contribute to the tangent shell-coupling at all.

Now take a general active mediator direction
\[
T_\star=\sum_{a=1}^8 c_a T^a,
\qquad
c_a\in\mathbb R.
\]
Then
\[
t_{10}(T_\star)=\frac12(c_1+i c_2),
\qquad
t_{20}(T_\star)=\frac12(c_4+i c_5).
\]

In the minimal shell-diagonal truncation, the shell-normal reduced \(J\)-matrix has the form
\[
U_\parallel
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\kappa_J t_{10}+\overline{\kappa_J t_{10}} & 0\\
0 & \kappa_J t_{20}+\overline{\kappa_J t_{20}}
\end{pmatrix}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
2\Re(\kappa_J t_{10}) & 0\\
0 & 2\Re(\kappa_J t_{20})
\end{pmatrix},
\]
where \(\kappa_J\neq0\) is the shell-normal Bragg prefactor coming from the derivative/harmonic projection.

Hence
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Bigr]
=
\Re\!\bigl[\kappa_J(t_{10}-t_{20})\bigr].
\]

Substituting the explicit canonical couplings,
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+i c_2)-(c_4+i c_5)\bigr)
\Bigr].
}
\]

Therefore the exact canonical vanishing condition is
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel=0
\iff
\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+i c_2)-(c_4+i c_5)\bigr)
\Bigr]=0.
}
\]

Equivalently, the longitudinal slot survives whenever the effective mediator direction has
unequal projected weight on the two coupling sectors
\[
\{T^1,T^2\}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\{T^4,T^5\},
\]
after the shell-normal phase \(\kappa_J\) is included.

Finally,
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3},
\]
so the explicit canonical sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq0,
\qquad
\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+i c_2)-(c_4+i c_5)\bigr)
\Bigr]\neq0.
}
\]

\section{Actual Generator-Level Computation of \texorpdfstring{$u_\parallel$}{u_parallel}}

\section{Step 1: canonical basis and active couplings}

Fix the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=e_1=
\begin{pmatrix}
1\\0\\0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u_1=e_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\1\\0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u_2=e_3=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\0\\1
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Let
\[
T^a=\frac{\lambda^a}{2}
\]
be the standard Hermitian \(SU(3)\) generators.
Then the shell-tangent couplings are
\[
t_{10}^a:=u_1^\dagger T^a z_0=(T^a)_{21},
\qquad
t_{20}^a:=u_2^\dagger T^a z_0=(T^a)_{31}.
\]

For the Gell-Mann basis one obtains:

\[
T^1=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1&0\\
1&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
t_{10}^{1}=\frac12,\qquad t_{20}^{1}=0,
\]

\[
T^2=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-i&0\\
i&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
t_{10}^{2}=\frac{i}{2},\qquad t_{20}^{2}=0,
\]

\[
T^3=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0&0\\
0&-1&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
t_{10}^{3}=0,\qquad t_{20}^{3}=0,
\]

\[
T^4=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&1\\
0&0&0\\
1&0&0
\end{pmatrix}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
t_{10}^{4}=0,\qquad t_{20}^{4}=\frac12,
\]

\[
T^5=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&-i\\
0&0&0\\
i&0&0
\end{pmatrix}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
t_{10}^{5}=0,\qquad t_{20}^{5}=\frac{i}{2},
\]

\[
T^6,\ T^7,\ T^8
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
t_{10}^{a}=t_{20}^{a}=0.
\]

So only
\[
T^1,\ T^2,\ T^4,\ T^5
\]
couple the locked direction \(z_0\) to the tangent doublet.

\section{Step 2: shell-normal reduced matrix}

In the minimal shell-diagonal truncation, define the shell-normal complex prefactor
\[
\kappa_J\neq0
\]
coming from the actual Bragg/harmonic/derivative projection.

Then the reduced shell-normal \(J\)-matrix is
\[
U_\parallel
=
\begin{pmatrix}
2\Re(\kappa_J t_{10}) & 0\\
0 & 2\Re(\kappa_J t_{20})
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Therefore
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Big[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Big]
=
\Re\!\bigl[\kappa_J(t_{10}-t_{20})\bigr].
\]

\section{Step 3: explicit single-generator values}

\subsection*{Case A: \(T_\star=T^1\)}

\[
t_{10}=\frac12,\qquad t_{20}=0,
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^1)=\frac12\,\Re(\kappa_J).
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
L_*(T^1)=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Re(\kappa_J),
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^1)
=
\frac14\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,\Re(\kappa_J)\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

\subsection*{Case B: \(T_\star=T^2\)}

\[
t_{10}=\frac{i}{2},\qquad t_{20}=0,
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^2)=\frac12\,\Re(i\kappa_J)=-\frac12\,\Im(\kappa_J).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
L_*(T^2)=-\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Im(\kappa_J),
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^2)
=
-\frac14\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,\Im(\kappa_J)\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

\subsection*{Case C: \(T_\star=T^4\)}

\[
t_{10}=0,\qquad t_{20}=\frac12,
\]
thus
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^4)=-\frac12\,\Re(\kappa_J).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
L_*(T^4)=-\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Re(\kappa_J),
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^4)
=
-\frac14\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,\Re(\kappa_J)\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

\subsection*{Case D: \(T_\star=T^5\)}

\[
t_{10}=0,\qquad t_{20}=\frac{i}{2},
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^5)=-\Re\!\left(\kappa_J\frac{i}{2}\right)
=
\frac12\,\Im(\kappa_J).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
L_*(T^5)=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Im(\kappa_J),
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^5)
=
\frac14\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,\Im(\kappa_J)\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

\subsection*{Case E: \(T_\star=T^3,T^6,T^7,T^8\)}

Since
\[
t_{10}=t_{20}=0,
\]
we get
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^3)=u_\parallel(T^6)=u_\parallel(T^7)=u_\parallel(T^8)=0.
}
\]
Therefore these directions do not produce a longitudinal \(J\)-split in the canonical locked basis.

\section{Step 4: generic active direction}

Take a general active mediator direction
\[
T_\star
=
c_1T^1+c_2T^2+c_4T^4+c_5T^5,
\qquad
c_i\in\mathbb R.
\]
Then
\[
t_{10}(T_\star)=\frac12(c_1+ic_2),
\qquad
t_{20}(T_\star)=\frac12(c_4+ic_5),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T_\star)
=
\frac12\,\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)
\Bigr].
}
\]

Hence the exact canonical vanishing condition is
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel=0
\iff
\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)
\Bigr]=0.
}
\]

\section{Step 5: explicit examples of cancellation and noncancellation}

\subsection*{Noncancelling example 1}
\[
T_\star=T^1
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
u_\parallel=\frac12\Re(\kappa_J).
\]
So if \(\Re(\kappa_J)\neq0\), longitudinal survival is immediate.

\subsection*{Noncancelling example 2}
\[
T_\star=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(T^1-T^4)
\]
gives
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}\Re(\kappa_J).
\]

\subsection*{Cancelling example}
\[
T_\star=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(T^1+T^4)
\]
gives
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Re\!\left[
\kappa_J\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt2}-\frac{1}{\sqrt2}\right)
\right]
=0.
\]
So exact equal shell-normal weight on the \(u_1\)- and \(u_2\)-coupling sectors produces longitudinal cancellation.

\section{Step 6: final witness condition}

Since
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3},
\]
the explicit canonical sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq0,
\qquad
\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)
\Bigr]\neq0.
}
\]

Under these conditions,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

In the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=e_1,\qquad u_1=e_2,\qquad u_2=e_3,
\]
the shell-tangent couplings are
\[
t_{10}^a=(T^a)_{21},
\qquad
t_{20}^a=(T^a)_{31}.
\]

For the standard \(SU(3)\) generators:
\[
T^1,T^2 \text{ couple only to }u_1,
\qquad
T^4,T^5 \text{ couple only to }u_2,
\]
while
\[
T^3,T^6,T^7,T^8
\]
do not couple the locked direction to the tangent doublet at all.

With shell-normal prefactor \(\kappa_J\), the reduced matrix is
\[
U_\parallel
=
\begin{pmatrix}
2\Re(\kappa_J t_{10}) & 0\\
0 & 2\Re(\kappa_J t_{20})
\end{pmatrix},
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\Re\!\bigl[\kappa_J(t_{10}-t_{20})\bigr].
}
\]

For a general active direction
\[
T_\star=c_1T^1+c_2T^2+c_4T^4+c_5T^5,
\]
this becomes
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)
\Bigr].
}
\]

Therefore the exact canonical cancellation condition is
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel=0
\iff
\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)
\Bigr]=0.
}
\]

So the longitudinal slot survives generically unless the mediator direction is tuned to give equal effective shell-normal weight on the two coupling sectors
\[
\{T^1,T^2\}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\{T^4,T^5\}.
\]

Finally,
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3},
\]
so the explicit canonical sufficient condition for longitudinal survival is
\[
\boxed{
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq0,
\qquad
\Re\!\Bigl[
\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)
\Bigr]\neq0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual single-generator computation of \(U_\parallel\), \(u_\parallel\), and \(\lambda_\parallel\)}

\section{Step 1: canonical basis}

Use the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=e_1,\qquad u_1=e_2,\qquad u_2=e_3.
\]
Then the shell-normal reduced \(J\)-matrix satisfies
\[
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\Bigr].
\]

Let the shell-normal projection prefactor be a complex scalar \(\kappa_J\).
For a single active generator \(T_\star\), the reduced diagonal entries are
\[
(U_\parallel)_{11}=2\Re(\kappa_J t_{10}),
\qquad
(U_\parallel)_{22}=2\Re(\kappa_J t_{20}),
\]
where
\[
t_{10}=u_1^\dagger T_\star z_0,
\qquad
t_{20}=u_2^\dagger T_\star z_0.
\]

\section{Step 2: explicit \(SU(3)\) couplings}

For \(T^a=\lambda^a/2\), the only nonzero canonical couplings are
\[
T^1:\quad t_{10}=\frac12,\ \ t_{20}=0,
\]
\[
T^2:\quad t_{10}=\frac{i}{2},\ \ t_{20}=0,
\]
\[
T^4:\quad t_{10}=0,\ \ t_{20}=\frac12,
\]
\[
T^5:\quad t_{10}=0,\ \ t_{20}=\frac{i}{2},
\]
while
\[
T^3,\ T^6,\ T^7,\ T^8
\]
have
\[
t_{10}=t_{20}=0.
\]

\section{Step 3: actual \(U_\parallel\) matrices}

\subsection*{Case A: \(T_\star=T^1\)}

\[
(U_\parallel)_{11}=2\Re\!\left(\kappa_J\frac12\right)=\Re(\kappa_J),
\qquad
(U_\parallel)_{22}=0.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
U_\parallel(T^1)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Re(\kappa_J) & 0\\
0 & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
\frac{\Re(\kappa_J)}{2}\mathbf 1_2
+
\frac{\Re(\kappa_J)}{2}\Sigma_3.
}
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^1)=\frac12\Re(\kappa_J).
}
\]

\subsection*{Case B: \(T_\star=T^2\)}

\[
(U_\parallel)_{11}=2\Re\!\left(\kappa_J\frac{i}{2}\right)=\Re(i\kappa_J)=-\Im(\kappa_J),
\qquad
(U_\parallel)_{22}=0.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
U_\parallel(T^2)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\Im(\kappa_J) & 0\\
0 & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
-\frac{\Im(\kappa_J)}{2}\mathbf 1_2
-
\frac{\Im(\kappa_J)}{2}\Sigma_3,
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^2)=-\frac12\Im(\kappa_J).
}
\]

\subsection*{Case C: \(T_\star=T^4\)}

\[
(U_\parallel)_{11}=0,
\qquad
(U_\parallel)_{22}=2\Re\!\left(\kappa_J\frac12\right)=\Re(\kappa_J).
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
U_\parallel(T^4)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & 0\\
0 & \Re(\kappa_J)
\end{pmatrix}
=
\frac{\Re(\kappa_J)}{2}\mathbf 1_2
-
\frac{\Re(\kappa_J)}{2}\Sigma_3,
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^4)=-\frac12\Re(\kappa_J).
}
\]

\subsection*{Case D: \(T_\star=T^5\)}

\[
(U_\parallel)_{11}=0,
\qquad
(U_\parallel)_{22}=2\Re\!\left(\kappa_J\frac{i}{2}\right)=-\Im(\kappa_J).
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
U_\parallel(T^5)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & 0\\
0 & -\Im(\kappa_J)
\end{pmatrix}
=
-\frac{\Im(\kappa_J)}{2}\mathbf 1_2
+
\frac{\Im(\kappa_J)}{2}\Sigma_3,
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^5)=\frac12\Im(\kappa_J).
}
\]

\subsection*{Case E: \(T_\star=T^3,T^6,T^7,T^8\)}

Since
\[
t_{10}=t_{20}=0,
\]
one gets
\[
\boxed{
U_\parallel=0,
\qquad
u_\parallel=0.
}
\]

\section{Step 4: actual \(L_*\) and \(\lambda_\parallel\)}

The canonical longitudinal invariant is
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\]
and under the minimal explicit specialization the reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

Since
\[
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
we get:

\subsection*{\(T_\star=T^1\)}
\[
\boxed{
L_*(T^1)=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Re(\kappa_J),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^1)
=
\frac14\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,\Re(\kappa_J)\,I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X m_\parallel \Re(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

\subsection*{\(T_\star=T^2\)}
\[
\boxed{
L_*(T^2)=-\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Im(\kappa_J),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^2)
=
-\frac14\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,\Im(\kappa_J)\,I_{\theta'^3}
=
+\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X m_\parallel \Im(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

\subsection*{\(T_\star=T^4\)}
\[
\boxed{
L_*(T^4)=-\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Re(\kappa_J),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^4)
=
-\frac14\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,\Re(\kappa_J)\,I_{\theta'^3}
=
+\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X m_\parallel \Re(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

\subsection*{\(T_\star=T^5\)}
\[
\boxed{
L_*(T^5)=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Im(\kappa_J),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^5)
=
\frac14\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,\Im(\kappa_J)\,I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X m_\parallel \Im(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

\section{Step 5: mixed active direction}

For a general active direction
\[
T_\star=c_1T^1+c_2T^2+c_4T^4+c_5T^5,
\qquad c_i\in\mathbb R,
\]
one has
\[
t_{10}=\frac12(c_1+ic_2),
\qquad
t_{20}=\frac12(c_4+ic_5),
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T_\star)
=
\frac12\Re\!\Bigl[\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)\Bigr].
}
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T_\star)
=
\frac14\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,
\Re\!\Bigl[\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)\Bigr]
\,I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

The exact cancellation locus is
\[
\boxed{
\Re\!\Bigl[\kappa_J\bigl((c_1+ic_2)-(c_4+ic_5)\bigr)\Bigr]=0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual explicit nondegenerate witness branch}

\section{1. Fix the longitudinal generator}

Take the active mediator direction to be
\[
\boxed{T_\star=T^1.}
\]

In the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=e_1,\qquad u_1=e_2,\qquad u_2=e_3,
\]
one has
\[
t_{10}=u_1^\dagger T^1 z_0=\frac12,
\qquad
t_{20}=u_2^\dagger T^1 z_0=0.
\]
Therefore the shell-normal reduced \(J\)-split is
\[
U_\parallel(T^1)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Re(\kappa_J) & 0\\
0 & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and hence
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^1)
=
\frac12\bigl[(U_\parallel)_{11}-(U_\parallel)_{22}\bigr]
=
\frac12\,\Re(\kappa_J).
}
\]

Thus
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
\alpha_X m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X m_\parallel \Re(\kappa_J).
}
\]

Using
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
we get
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^1)
=
\frac14\,\alpha_X m_\parallel \Re(\kappa_J)\,I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X m_\parallel \Re(\kappa_J)\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

\section{2. Fix the transverse seed}

Now choose the pure transverse \(E\)-direction in the explicit canonical split:
\[
\boxed{
\xi_Ev_E=1,
\qquad
\xi_Ov_O=0.
}
\]
Then
\[
c_E=\beta_X,
\qquad
c_O=0.
\]
Using
\[
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\]
we obtain
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\beta_X I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\]

Thus the reduced first-order symbol is
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel(T^1)\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
-
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\,
(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
}
\]

\section{3. Exact determinant}

Since
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2),
\]
for this branch we get
\[
\det M
=
\lambda_\parallel(T^1)\,\alpha^2.
\]
Now
\[
\alpha^2
=
\left(\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\right)^2
=
\frac{3\pi^2}{256}\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\det M
=
-\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{262144}\,
\alpha_X\beta_X^2\,m_\parallel\,\Re(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}
\]

Therefore the explicit sufficient condition for a nondegenerate Weyl/Dirac witness in this branch is
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\Re(\kappa_J)\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\]
Under these conditions,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha\neq0,
\qquad
\beta=0,
\qquad
\det M\neq0.
}
\]

\section{4. Pure \(O\)-branch variant}

If instead we choose
\[
\xi_Ev_E=0,
\qquad
\xi_Ov_O=1,
\]
then
\[
\alpha=0,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\]
while the same \(\lambda_\parallel(T^1)\) survives.
Hence
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(T^1)\beta^2
\]
and the same nondegeneracy condition follows.

\section{5. Honest interpretation}

This does \emph{not} prove that the full complete microscopic TECT action has already been executed at the final transverse derivative-bookkeeping level.

What it does prove is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item inside the explicit canonical split, there exists a fully concrete branch with
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
\det M\neq0;
\]

\item the longitudinal part is realized by the actual internal generator choice \(T_\star=T^1\);

\item the transverse part is realized by the explicit \(E\)- or \(O\)-seed direction of the already fixed seed space.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Explicit completion of the canonical witness branch \(T_\star=T^1\)}

\section{1. Longitudinal part}

In the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=e_1,\qquad u_1=e_2,\qquad u_2=e_3,
\]
the active generator \(T_\star=T^1\) has
\[
t_{10}=u_1^\dagger T^1 z_0=\frac12,
\qquad
t_{20}=u_2^\dagger T^1 z_0=0.
\]
Hence the shell-normal reduced \(J\)-split is
\[
u_\parallel(T^1)=\frac12\,\Re(\kappa_J).
\]
Therefore
\[
L_*(T^1)=m_\parallel u_\parallel(T^1)=\frac{m_\parallel}{2}\Re(\kappa_J).
\]

Using the exact reduced longitudinal formula
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,I_{\theta'^3},
\]
together with
\[
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^1)
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel\,\Re(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:T1_lambda_final}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Transverse part}

Now choose the pure \(E\)-seed direction
\[
R_\perp=1,
\qquad
\varphi=0.
\]
Then the transverse part of the master symbol reduces to
\[
\beta_X I_\theta(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2),
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\beta_X I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:T1_alpha_beta_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full reduced first-order symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X m_\parallel \Re(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,
p_\parallel\sigma_3
-
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\,
(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:T1_A1_final}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Determinant and nondegeneracy}

The reduced Weyl determinant is
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\]
Since \(\beta=0\), this becomes
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel\alpha^2.
\]
Now
\[
\alpha^2
=
\left(\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\right)^2
=
\frac{3\pi^2}{256}\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
\]
Substituting \eqref{eq:T1_lambda_final},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
-\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{262144}\,
\alpha_X\beta_X^2\,m_\parallel\,\Re(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}
\label{eq:T1_det_final}
\end{equation}

Hence an explicit sufficient condition for nondegeneracy is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\Re(\kappa_J)\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\label{eq:T1_nondeg_cond}
\end{equation}
Under these conditions,
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha\neq0,
\qquad
\det M\neq0.
\]

\section{4. Infrared velocities}

The reduced velocities are
\[
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{IR}}=|\lambda_\parallel|,
\qquad
v_\perp^{\mathrm{IR}}=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}=|\alpha|.
\]
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{IR}}(T^1)
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
|\alpha_X m_\parallel \Re(\kappa_J)|\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:T1_vpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp^{\mathrm{IR}}(T^1)
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
|\beta_X|\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:T1_vperp}
\end{equation}

Therefore the anisotropy ratio is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho(T^1)
=
\frac{v_\parallel^{\mathrm{IR}}}{v_\perp^{\mathrm{IR}}}
=
\frac{3}{64}\,
\frac{|\alpha_X|}{|\beta_X|}\,
|m_\parallel\Re(\kappa_J)|\,
\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
}
\label{eq:T1_rho}
\end{equation}
up to the overall sign convention.

\section{5. Pure \(O\)-variant}

If instead one chooses
\[
R_\perp=1,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{2},
\]
then
\[
\alpha=0,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\]
while the same \(\lambda_\parallel(T^1)\) survives.
Hence the determinant becomes
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel\beta^2,
\]
with exactly the same nondegeneracy condition
\eqref{eq:T1_nondeg_cond}.

\section{6. Final explicit verdict for this branch}

The branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad R_\perp=1,\qquad \varphi=0
}
\]
is a fully explicit finite witness branch.

Its reduced coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{1024}\,
\alpha_X m_\parallel \Re(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0,
}
\]
and its determinant is
\[
\boxed{
\det M
=
-\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{262144}\,
\alpha_X\beta_X^2\,m_\parallel\,\Re(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}
\]

Therefore this branch is nondegenerate whenever
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,\quad
\beta_X\neq0,\quad
m_\parallel\neq0,\quad
\Re(\kappa_J)\neq0,\quad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

A fully explicit finite nondegenerate witness branch is obtained by choosing
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad R_\perp=1,\qquad \varphi=0.
}
\]

Then
\[
u_\parallel(T^1)=\frac12\Re(\kappa_J),
\qquad

and therefore

For the pure \(E\)-transverse seed,

\qquad
\beta=0.
}

Hence

\boxed{

=
-\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{262144}\,
\alpha_X\beta_X^2\,m_\parallel\,\Re(\kappa_J)\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}

So the branch is nondegenerate whenever

\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,\quad
\beta_X\neq0,\quad
m_\parallel\neq0,\quad
\Re(\kappa_J)\neq0,\quad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\]

Thus one explicit witness branch is already completely finite and concrete.
The only remaining unresolved microscopic input is the actual refined locked Bloch value of
\[
\Re(\kappa_J).

\section{Elimination of the auxiliary \texorpdfstring{$\kappa_J$}{kappaJ} and exact closure of the \(T_\star=T^1\) witness branch}

\section{1. Scalar reduction of the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal factor}

The current refined locked \(+\) Class II notes imply that the principal pure-\(JJ\) axial tensor has the isotropic shell form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{jm}^{(JJ)}=\Xi_{JJ}\,\delta_{jm}.
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_CJJ}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n\cdot C^{(JJ)}G_*=\Xi_{JJ}|G_*|.
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_contract}
\end{equation}

In the canonical locked basis and minimal explicit Class II split,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{JJ}=\mathcal N_{JJ}L_*,
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_XiJJ}
\end{equation}
Therefore the first-shell Fourier coefficient becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)
=
i\,\mathcal N_{JJ}\,L_*\,|G_*|\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_Ahat}
\end{equation}

This shows that the previously introduced shell-normal prefactor \(\kappa_J\) is not an independent microscopic datum.
Its shell-relevant role is completely absorbed into the scalar reduction factor
\[
\mathcal N_{JJ}|G_*|A_{G_*}.
\]

\section{2. Canonical \(T_\star=T^1\) branch}

Fix the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=e_1,\qquad u_1=e_2,\qquad u_2=e_3.
\]
Take the active mediator direction
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1.
}
\]
Then
\[
t_{10}=u_1^\dagger T^1 z_0=\frac12,
\qquad
t_{20}=u_2^\dagger T^1 z_0=0.
\]
Therefore the shell-normal \(J\)-singlet bias is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_\parallel(T^1)\neq 0
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_upar_nonzero}
\end{equation}
whenever the canonical \(J\)-kernel is not tuned to equalize the two tangent channels.

Equivalently, the remaining longitudinal scalar is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*(T^1)=m_\parallel u_\parallel(T^1).
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_Lstar}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Pure longitudinal Fourier coefficient}

Substituting \eqref{eq:kappa_elim_Lstar} into \eqref{eq:kappa_elim_Ahat},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*;T^1)
=
i\,\mathcal N_{JJ}\,m_\parallel u_\parallel(T^1)\,|G_*|\,A_{G_*}.
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_Ahat_T1}
\end{equation}

Hence, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
u_\parallel(T^1)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_four_conditions}
\end{equation}
then
\[
\widehat{\mathcal A}_{JJ}(G_*)\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\widehat V_\parallel^{(JJ)}(G_*)\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
\]

\section{4. Exact longitudinal coefficient}

Inside the exact Branch-B reduced dictionary,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,I_{\theta'^3}\,\lambda_c^{(JJ)},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_lamdict}
\end{equation}

The pure-\(JJ\) carrier-side scalar is already reduced to \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\) up to the fixed microscopic normalization.
So introduce the explicit branch-normalization constant
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(JJ)}=\Gamma_{JJ}\,m_\parallel u_\parallel(T^1),
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_GammaJJ}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\Gamma_{JJ}
\]
is the fixed shell/Bloch normalization determined by the projected refined locked basis.
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(T^1)
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\Gamma_{JJ}\,
m_\parallel u_\parallel(T^1)\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_lambda_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, using \eqref{eq:kappa_elim_Ahat_T1}, one may regard
\[
\Gamma_{JJ}\propto \alpha_X\mathcal N_{JJ}|G_*|A_{G_*}
\]
in the first-shell dominant microscopic reduction.

\section{5. Explicit transverse completion}

Choose the pure transverse \(E\)-seed:
\[
R_\perp=1,
\qquad
\varphi=0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
I_\theta\,\beta_X
=

\qquad
\beta=0,
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_transverse}
\end{equation}
where
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.

Therefore the reduced first-order symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel(T^1)\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
-
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\,
(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_symbol}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Exact determinant}

Since
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2),
\]
and \(\beta=0\), we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
\lambda_\parallel(T^1)\,
\left(\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\right)^2.
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_det1}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:kappa_elim_lambda_final},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
-\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{131072}\,
\Gamma_{JJ}\,\beta_X^2\,
m_\parallel u_\parallel(T^1)\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_det2}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact explicit sufficient condition for this branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_{JJ}\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
m_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
u_\parallel(T^1)\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\label{eq:kappa_elim_suff}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Final practical meaning}

The previous notation \(\Re(\kappa_J)\) is not needed anymore.
The true microscopic longitudinal input is
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\]
and its shell/Fourier promotion is controlled by
\[
\mathcal N_{JJ}|G_*|A_{G_*},
\]
equivalently by the one fixed branch normalization \(\Gamma_{JJ}\).

So the explicit canonical branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad R_\perp=1,\qquad \varphi=0
\]
is completely finite once the following scalars are inserted:
\[
m_\parallel,\qquad
u_\parallel(T^1),\qquad
A_{G_*},\qquad
\mathcal N_{JJ}\ \ (\text{equiv.\ }\Gamma_{JJ}),\qquad
\beta_X.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The auxiliary notation \(\kappa_J\) is not needed as an independent microscopic input.

In the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the pure-\(JJ\) longitudinal tensor collapses to
\[
C_{jm}^{(JJ)}=\Xi_{JJ}\delta_{jm},
\]

\Xi_{JJ}=\mathcal N_{JJ}L_*,

m_\parallel,\qquad
u_\parallel,\qquad

For the explicit canonical witness branch

with \(\Gamma_{JJ}\propto \alpha_X\mathcal N_{JJ}|G_*|A_{G_*}\) in the first-shell dominant reduction.

Therefore an explicit sufficient condition for a nondegenerate witness branch is

\Gamma_{JJ}\neq0,\qquad

m_\parallel\neq0,\qquad
u_\parallel(T^1)\neq0,\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.

Under these conditions,

\section{Direct completion of the explicit branch in the latest acceptance-stage normalization}

Choose
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
R_\perp=1,
\qquad
\varphi=0.
}
\]

Then the longitudinal coefficient is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3.
