\label{eq:latest_lambda}
\end{equation}
Using
\[
I_3=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
C_\parallel\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:latest_lambda_explicit}
\end{equation}

The transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:latest_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced first-order symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
C_\parallel\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,
p_\parallel\sigma_3
-
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\,
(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:latest_symbol}
\end{equation}

Since
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2),
\]
and \(\beta=0\), one gets
\[
\alpha^2
=
\frac{3\pi^2}{256}\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{131072}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X^3}{M_X^2}\,
C_\parallel\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}
\label{eq:latest_det}
\end{equation}

So the exact sufficient condition for this branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\label{eq:latest_suff}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, since
\[
C_\parallel\neq0
\iff
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}\neq(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22},
\]
the condition can be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}\neq(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22},
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\label{eq:latest_suff_diag}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Direct diagonal-difference completion of the explicit witness branch}

\section{1. Define the actual remaining longitudinal scalar}

Introduce the exact projected diagonal difference
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel
:=
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}
-
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}.
}
\label{eq:DWpar_def}
\end{equation}
Then the reduced longitudinal coefficient is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\Delta W_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:DWpar_lambda}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the Branch-B one-mediator normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3,
\qquad
I_3
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:DWpar_branchB}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X I_3}\,\Delta W_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:DWpar_Cpar}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Fix the transverse branch}

Choose the explicit pure-\(E\) transverse seed
\[
R_\perp=1,
\qquad
\varphi=0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:DWpar_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced first-order symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac12\,\Delta W_\parallel\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
-
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\,
(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:DWpar_symbol}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact determinant}

Since
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2),
\]
and \(\beta=0\), we get
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel\alpha^2.
\]
Now
\[
\alpha^2
=
\left(\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa\right)^2
=
\frac{3\pi^2}{256}\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
\]
Substituting \eqref{eq:DWpar_lambda},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
\frac{3\pi^2}{512}\,
\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2\,
\Delta W_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:DWpar_det_direct}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:DWpar_branchB}, the same determinant may also be written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{131072}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X^3}{M_X^2}\,
C_\parallel\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}
\label{eq:DWpar_det_Cpar}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact nondegeneracy condition for this explicit branch}

Therefore the branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad R_\perp=1,\qquad \varphi=0
}
\]
is nondegenerate iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq 0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:DWpar_nondeg_direct}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the one-mediator calibration language,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\label{eq:DWpar_nondeg_Cpar}
\end{equation}

\section{5. If the scalar core remains diagonal-symmetric}

The exact longitudinal split formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\lambda_\parallel
=
\bigl(D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2\bigr)
-
\bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:DWpar_split}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel
=
\bigl(D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2\bigr)
-
\bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:DWpar_split2}
\end{equation}

So, if the explicit safe scalar core/refined tree-level block remains diagonal-symmetric,
\[
D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2=0,
\]
then the entire longitudinal decision reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel
=
-\bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:DWpar_mediated_only}
\end{equation}

In that case, the working-branch Gate-2 question is literally the sign/nonvanishing of the mediated diagonal asymmetry.

\section{6. Final explicit verdict}

Thus the actual explicit branch calculation is already compressed to one scalar:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel
=
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}
-
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}.
}
\label{eq:DWpar_finalscalar}
\end{equation}

Once this is computed from the projected refined locked Bloch operator, everything else follows immediately:
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Delta W_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0,
\]
and
\[
\det M
=
\frac{3\pi^2}{512}\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2\,\Delta W_\parallel.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

For the explicit witness branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad R_\perp=1,\qquad \varphi=0,
}
\]
the remaining longitudinal microscopic input is the single projected diagonal difference
\[
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel
=
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}
-
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}.
}
\]

The reduced coefficients are then exactly
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\Delta W_\parallel,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\]

Hence the determinant is
\[
\boxed{
\det M
=
\frac{3\pi^2}{512}\,
\beta_X^2\theta_0^2\kappa^2\,
\Delta W_\parallel.
}
\]

Equivalently, using the one-mediator Branch-B calibration,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3,
\qquad
C_\parallel
=
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X I_3}\,\Delta W_\parallel.
}
\]

Therefore the exact nondegeneracy condition for this explicit branch is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0,
}
\]
or equivalently
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\]

So the entire remaining Gate-2 bottleneck is now the direct projected matrix-element computation of
\[
\boxed{
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}
-
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual diagonal-difference computation for the explicit branch \(T_\star=T^1\)}

\section{1. Exact split}

The exact longitudinal split is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\lambda_\parallel
=
\Bigl(D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2\Bigr)
-
\Bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_split}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel
:=
(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{11}-(\hat n\!\cdot\!\vec W_+)_{22}
=
\Bigl(D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2\Bigr)
-
\Bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:actual_DW}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,\Delta W_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:actual_lambda_DW}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Tree-level core contribution}

In the present safe scalar/refined-tree branch, the direct amplitude/scalar sector contributes only to the identity channel, and the direct projector-stiffness tree level contributes zero to the traceless transport kernel.

Therefore, in the current explicit tree-level branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2=0.
}
\label{eq:actual_D0_zero}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact longitudinal coefficient reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\lambda_\parallel
=
-\Bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_lambda_medonly}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Mediated response matrix}

The mediated quadratic response in the adapted frame is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\overline{\mathcal C_{ia;m}}\,
\mathcal C_{ia;n},
}
\label{eq:actual_rmed}
\end{equation}
so the longitudinal Pauli component is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}
=
\frac12\bigl(r_{11}^{\mathrm{med}}-r_{22}^{\mathrm{med}}\bigr)
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}
\left[
\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal C_{ia;1}|^2
-
\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal C_{ia;2}|^2
\right].
}
\label{eq:actual_s3med}
\end{equation}

Thus a sufficient condition for a nonzero mediated longitudinal channel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal C_{ia;1}|^2
\neq
\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal C_{ia;2}|^2.
}
\label{eq:actual_long_suff}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Explicit canonical branch \(T_\star=T^1\)}

Take the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=e_1,\qquad u_1=e_2,\qquad u_2=e_3,
\]
and choose the active mediator direction
\[
\boxed{T_\star=T^1.}
\]

Then
\[
t_{10}=u_1^\dagger T^1 z_0=\frac12,
\qquad
t_{20}=u_2^\dagger T^1 z_0=0.
\]

In the minimal single-generator shell truncation, this means that the mediated current amplitudes take the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{ia;1}=\frac12\,\mathcal A_{ia},
\qquad
\mathcal C_{ia;2}=0,
}
\label{eq:actual_C_T1}
\end{equation}
for some shell-normal amplitude family \(\mathcal A_{ia}\) determined by the actual background-linear cross term.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal C_{ia;1}|^2
=
\frac14\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal A_{ia}|^2,
\qquad
\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal C_{ia;2}|^2=0.
\label{eq:actual_Csum_T1}
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma_J^{(T^1)}
:=
\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal A_{ia}|^2.
}
\label{eq:actual_SigmaJ}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}(T^1)
=
-\frac{1}{8M_X^2}\Sigma_J^{(T^1)}.
}
\label{eq:actual_s3_T1}
\end{equation}

As long as the shell/background-linear cross term is not identically zero,
\[
\Sigma_J^{(T^1)}>0,
\]
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}(T^1)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:actual_s3_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Diagonal-difference and longitudinal coefficient}

Since the current explicit branch has \(D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2=0\), the whole diagonal difference is mediated:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel
=
-
\Bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_DW_med}
\end{equation}

Introduce the positive shell-normal mediated diagonal asymmetry
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta D_{\mathrm{med}}^{(T^1)}
:=
D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2
=
\frac{1}{4M_X^2}\Sigma_J^{(T^1)},
}
\label{eq:actual_Dmed_T1}
\end{equation}
up to the fixed transport-normalization convention relating \(D^{(\mathrm{med})}\) to the adapted response matrix.

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel^{(T^1)}
=
-\Delta D_{\mathrm{med}}^{(T^1)},
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel^{(T^1)}
=
-\frac12\Delta D_{\mathrm{med}}^{(T^1)}.
}
\label{eq:actual_lambda_T1}
\end{equation}

Therefore, provided the shell/background-linear cross term is active,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel^{(T^1)}\neq0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel^{(T^1)}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:actual_lambda_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Transverse completion of the same branch}

Now choose the pure \(E\)-transverse seed
\[
R_\perp=1,
\qquad
\varphi=0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:actual_alpha_T1}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
\lambda_\parallel^{(T^1)}\,\alpha^2.
}
\label{eq:actual_det_T1}
\end{equation}
So if
\[
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0,
\qquad
\Sigma_J^{(T^1)}>0,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:actual_det_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Final explicit verdict}

Thus, in the explicit branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad R_\perp=1,\qquad \varphi=0,
}
\]
the tree-level core contribution to the diagonal difference vanishes,
while the mediated block gives a nonzero diagonal asymmetry as soon as the actual shell/background-linear current amplitude is nontrivial.

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel^{(T^1)}
=
-
\Bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\Bigr)
\neq0
}
\label{eq:actual_branch_result}
\end{equation}
under the finite condition
\[
\Sigma_J^{(T^1)}>0.
\]

Hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha\neq0,
\qquad
\beta=0,
\qquad
\det M\neq0
\]
for this branch.

\section{Actual completion of the explicit \(T_\star=T^1\) branch}

The exact longitudinal split is
\[
2\lambda_\parallel
=
\bigl(D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2\bigr)
-
\bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\bigr).
\]
In the present safe scalar tree branch,
\[
D^{(0)}_1-D^{(0)}_2=0,
\]
so
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac12\bigl(D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2\bigr).
\]

Take the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=e_1,\qquad u_1=e_2,\qquad u_2=e_3,
\]
and choose the active generator
\[
T_\star=T^1.
\]
Then
\[
t_{10}=u_1^\dagger T^1 z_0=\frac12,
\qquad
t_{20}=u_2^\dagger T^1 z_0=0.
\]
Hence, in the minimal single-generator shell truncation,
\[
\mathcal C_{ia;1}=\frac12\,\mathcal A_{ia},
\qquad
\mathcal C_{ia;2}=0.
\]

Using
\[
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}\overline{\mathcal C_{ia;m}}\mathcal C_{ia;n},
\]
we get
\[
r_{11}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac1{4M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal A_{ia}|^2,
\qquad
r_{22}^{\mathrm{med}}=0,
\qquad
r_{12}^{\mathrm{med}}=0.
\]
Define
\[
\Sigma_J^{(T^1)}:=\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal A_{ia}|^2.
\]
Then
\[
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}
=
\frac12(r_{11}^{\mathrm{med}}-r_{22}^{\mathrm{med}})
=
-\frac{1}{8M_X^2}\Sigma_J^{(T^1)}.
\]

Let \(\nu_\parallel>0\) be the fixed transport normalization relating the mediated response to the diagonal derivative split. Then
\[
D^{(\mathrm{med})}_1-D^{(\mathrm{med})}_2
=
-\frac{\nu_\parallel}{4M_X^2}\Sigma_J^{(T^1)},
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
\Delta W_\parallel^{(T^1)}
=
\frac{\nu_\parallel}{4M_X^2}\Sigma_J^{(T^1)},
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel^{(T^1)}
=
\frac{\nu_\parallel}{8M_X^2}\Sigma_J^{(T^1)}.
}
\]

Now choose the pure even transverse seed
\[
R_\perp=1,\qquad \varphi=0.
\]
Then
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\beta_X\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\det M
=
\frac{3\pi^2}{2048}\,
\frac{\nu_\parallel\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\Sigma_J^{(T^1)}\,
\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
}
\]

Therefore, as long as
\[
\beta_X\neq0,\qquad \theta_0\kappa\neq0,\qquad \Sigma_J^{(T^1)}>0,
\]
the explicit branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad R_\perp=1,\qquad \varphi=0
}
\]
satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,\qquad
\alpha\neq0,\qquad
\beta=0,\qquad
\det M\neq0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Canonical Branch and Continued Coefficient Extraction}

\section{Short explanation}

We adopt the canonical explicit one-mediator normalization
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
and use the one-mediator transport-side coefficient point
\[
\lambda_c^{(1)}=-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}=-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}=-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
\]

The defect overlaps are
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]

We now fix the explicit witness branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=1,
\qquad
\gamma_O=0,
}
\]
so that the transverse sector is purely even.

\section{1. Reduced coefficients}

Using
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\widetilde\Lambda_O,
\]
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:branch_lambda_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:branch_ab_general}
\end{equation}

For the explicit pure-\(E\) choice \(\gamma_E=1,\gamma_O=0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:branch_ab_Eonly}
\end{equation}

Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
\approx
0.03188319195\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^3,
}
\label{eq:branch_lambda_num}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
\approx
0.34008738079\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:branch_alpha_num}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Determinant}

Since
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2),
\]
the explicit pure-\(E\) branch gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{131072}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X^3}{M_X^6}\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5.
}
\label{eq:branch_det_final}
\end{equation}
Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
\approx
0.003687591698\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X^3}{M_X^6}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^5.
}
\label{eq:branch_det_num}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit sufficient condition for a nondegenerate reduced symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\label{eq:branch_nondeg_cond}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Transport/Bloch coefficients}

Because \(C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1\), the exact dictionary becomes
\[
g_c=\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E=\alpha,
\qquad
g_O=\beta.
\]
Hence, in the explicit pure-\(E\) branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:branch_gc}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:branch_gego}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Continued coefficient-finding: radial core coefficients}

Under the matching hypothesis
\[
g_E^{\rm core}=\xi_E g_E,
\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}=\xi_c g_c,
\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}=\xi_O g_O,
\]
the radial coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0
=
\frac{1}{z_{0,0}}
\bigl(
\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c
\bigr),
\qquad
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0
=
\frac{\xi_O g_O}{z_{0,0}}.
}
\label{eq:branch_a0b0c0}
\end{equation}

In the explicit pure-\(E\) branch, \(g_O=0\), so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_0=0.
}
\label{eq:branch_c0_zero}
\end{equation}
Moreover,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:branch_b0}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0
=
b_0(1+R_c),
}
\label{eq:branch_a0_from_Rc}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{\alpha}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:branch_Rc}
\end{equation}

Thus the explicit branch-level radial coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
a_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa
\left[
1+\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\right],
\qquad
c_0=0.
}
\label{eq:branch_radial_coeffs_final}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Radial one-mode criterion in this branch}

The practical compact criterion for the important case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,\qquad \kappa_{\rm comp}\ge 1
\]
is
\[
-1<R_c<1,\qquad \alpha>0,\qquad \mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

Substituting \eqref{eq:branch_Rc}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2
<1,
}
\label{eq:branch_Rc_window}
\end{equation}
together with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:branch_rest_criterion}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Unit benchmark}

For the canonical unit benchmark
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=1,\ \gamma_O=0,
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
\approx
0.03188319195\,(\theta_0\kappa)^3,
}
\label{eq:bench_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
\approx
0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
\beta=0,
}
\label{eq:bench_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
\approx
0.003687591698\,(\theta_0\kappa)^5,
}
\label{eq:bench_det}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,0.09375\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:bench_Rc}
\end{equation}

Hence, in the natural small-defect regime \((\theta_0\kappa)^2\ll1\), one has
\[
|R_c|\ll 1
\]
for \(O(1)\) matching constants \(\xi_c,\xi_E\).
So the radial one-mode inequality is naturally satisfied away from accidental sign failures in \(\mu_\infty\) and the remote-gap condition.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Radial Coefficient Continuation for the Explicit Branch \texorpdfstring{$T_\star=T^1$}{T*=T1}}

\section{Short explanation}

We now continue the coefficient-finding program by inserting the explicit Bloch/Class-II branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0
\]
into the radial one-mode dictionary.

The branch-level Bloch coefficients are already fixed as
\[
g_c=\lambda_\parallel,\qquad g_E=\alpha,\qquad g_O=\beta
\]
in the current canonical normalization \(C_c=C_E=C_O=1\).

For the explicit pure-\(E\) branch,
\[
g_O=0,
\]
so the odd core coefficient vanishes identically and the remaining radial parameters reduce to
\[
a_0,\qquad b_0,\qquad R_c,\qquad \mu_\infty.
\]

\section{1. Branch input from the explicit transport calculation}

For the explicit branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
}
\]
the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:radial_branch_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:radial_branch_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
\approx
0.03188319195\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^3,
}
\label{eq:radial_branch_lambda_num}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
\approx
0.34008738079\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:radial_branch_alpha_num}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Matching dictionary to core coefficients}

Introduce the matching constants
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E^{\rm core}=\xi_E g_E,
\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}=\xi_c g_c,
\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}=\xi_O g_O,
\qquad
\xi_E,\xi_c,\xi_O>0.
}
\label{eq:radial_matching}
\end{equation}
Then the exact core coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}+g_c^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{g_O^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}}.
}
\label{eq:radial_a0b0c0_dict}
\end{equation}

Using \(g_c=\lambda_\parallel\), \(g_E=\alpha\), \(g_O=\beta\), one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0
=
\frac{1}{z_{0,0}}
\bigl(
\xi_E\alpha+\xi_c\lambda_\parallel
\bigr),
\qquad
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\alpha,
\qquad
c_0
=
\frac{\xi_O}{z_{0,0}}\beta.
}
\label{eq:radial_a0b0c0_branch}
\end{equation}

Since the explicit branch has \(\beta=0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_0=0.
}
\label{eq:radial_c0_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Explicit formulas for \texorpdfstring{$b_0$}{b0} and \texorpdfstring{$a_0$}{a0}}

Substituting \eqref{eq:radial_branch_alpha_beta} into \eqref{eq:radial_a0b0c0_branch},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:radial_b0_exact}
\end{equation}
Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0
\approx
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
0.34008738079\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa).
}
\label{eq:radial_b0_num}
\end{equation}

Similarly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa
+
\frac{\xi_c}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:radial_a0_exact}
\end{equation}
Factorizing \(b_0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
}
\label{eq:radial_a0_factor}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
:=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{\alpha}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:radial_Rc_exact}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa
\left[
1+\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\right].
}
\label{eq:radial_a0_final}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Sign conditions}

Because \(\xi_E>0\) and \(z_{0,0}>0\) by convention, the sign of \(b_0\) is the sign of \(\alpha\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0>0
\iff
\alpha>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0.
}
\label{eq:radial_b0_positive}
\end{equation}

Likewise,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0>0
\iff
b_0>0
\ \text{and}\ 
1+R_c>0.
}
\label{eq:radial_a0_positive}
\end{equation}

Since \(c_0=0\), there is no odd/torsion-like phase contribution in this branch.

\section{5. One-mode criterion in the practical lowest-channel case}

In the practically most relevant case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,\qquad \kappa_{\rm comp}\ge 1,
\]
the sufficient criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:radial_practical_criterion}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:radial_Rc_exact}, the first inequality becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2
<1.
}
\label{eq:radial_Rc_window}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire core-side acceptance problem for this branch reduces to checking:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
\qquad
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2
\right|<1.
}
\label{eq:radial_branch_checklist}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Bulk mass parameter}

The bulk mass parameter is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\label{eq:radial_muinf_general}
\end{equation}
In the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\label{eq:radial_muinf_vac}
\end{equation}
Hence, if \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\) is fixed by convention, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:radial_muinf_sign}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Unit benchmark}

For the canonical unit benchmark
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=1,
\qquad
\xi_E=\xi_c=1,
\qquad
z_{0,0}=1,
\qquad
\chi_\infty=0,
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0
\approx
0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa),
}
\label{eq:radial_b0_bench}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
0.09375\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
}
\label{eq:radial_Rc_bench}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0
\approx
0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa)\,
\bigl[1+0.09375(\theta_0\kappa)^2\bigr].
}
\label{eq:radial_a0_bench}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_0=0.
}
\label{eq:radial_c0_bench}
\end{equation}

Therefore in the small-defect regime \((\theta_0\kappa)^2\ll1\),
\[
|R_c|\ll 1,
\]
so the condition \(-1<R_c<1\) is automatically satisfied for this benchmark branch.

\section{8. Honest status}

For the explicit branch \(T_\star=T^1,\gamma_E=1,\gamma_O=0\), the following are now explicit:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(g_c,g_E,g_O\);
\item \(a_0,b_0,c_0\) in terms of \(\xi_E,\xi_c,z_{0,0}\);
\item the exact benchmark ratio \(R_c\);
\item the reduction of the one-mode criterion to the four checks
\[
R_c,\ \alpha,\ \mu_\infty,\ \Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

What remains genuinely branch-specific is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual matching constants \(\xi_E,\xi_c\);
\item the actual bulk mass sign \(\mu_\infty\);
\item the actual remote-gap inequality.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

For the explicit canonical branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
}
\]
the Bloch/Class-II coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
g_c=\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
g_E=\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=\beta=0.
}
\]

Using the exact matching dictionary
\[
g_E^{\rm core}=\xi_E g_E,\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}=\xi_c g_c,\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}=\xi_O g_O,
\]
the radial core coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
c_0=0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
\qquad
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
b_0>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
a_0>0
\iff
b_0>0\ \text{and}\ 1+R_c>0.
}
\]

In the practically most relevant lowest-channel case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,\qquad \kappa_{\rm comp}\ge 1,
\]
the sufficient one-mode criterion reduces to
\[
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

For the canonical unit benchmark
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=\xi_E=\xi_c=z_{0,0}=1,
\qquad
\chi_\infty=0,
\]
one gets
\[
\boxed{
b_0
\approx
0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
R_c
=
0.09375\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
a_0
\approx
0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa)\,
\bigl[1+0.09375(\theta_0\kappa)^2\bigr],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
c_0=0.
}
\]

Thus, for this explicit branch, the remaining coefficient-finding problem has been reduced to the finite branch data
\[
\boxed{
\xi_E,\qquad \xi_c,\qquad \mu_\infty,\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

\section{Continued explicit coefficient-finding for the canonical branch}

\section{Short explanation}

For the explicit branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
\]
the transport-side coefficients are already fixed at the working-branch level:
\[
g_c=\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E=\alpha,
\qquad
g_O=0.
\]
Therefore the radial problem reduces to
\[
a_0,\qquad b_0,\qquad c_0=0,\qquad R_c,\qquad \mu_\infty.
\]

\section{1. Branch input}

Using the already extracted explicit branch coefficients,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:cont_gc}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:cont_gego}
\end{equation}

Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c
\approx
0.03188319195\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^3,
}
\label{eq:cont_gc_num}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E
\approx
0.34008738079\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:cont_ge_num}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact radial coefficients}

The exact constitutive dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{\xi_O g_O}{z_{0,0}}.
}
\label{eq:cont_a0b0c0}
\end{equation}
Since \(g_O=0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_0=0.
}
\label{eq:cont_c0_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:cont_b0}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa
+
\frac{\xi_c}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:cont_a0}
\end{equation}

Factorizing \(b_0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
}
\label{eq:cont_a0_factor}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{g_c}{g_E}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:cont_Rc}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Immediate sign consequences}

Assume the standard convention
\[
z_{0,0}>0,\qquad \xi_E>0,\qquad \xi_c>0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0.
}
\label{eq:cont_b0_sign}
\end{equation}

Similarly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0>0
\iff
b_0>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
1+R_c>0.
}
\label{eq:cont_a0_sign}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Practical one-mode window}

In the practically most relevant case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,\qquad \kappa_{\rm comp}\ge 1,
\]
the sufficient criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:cont_practical}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:cont_Rc},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3\,|\alpha_X|\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2}.
}
\label{eq:cont_ratio_bound}
\end{equation}

So the entire low-core inequality is reduced to a finite ratio bound on \(\xi_c/\xi_E\).

\section{5. Explicit benchmark values for the ratio window}

Under the unit benchmark
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=\xi_E=z_{0,0}=1,
\]
the ratio window becomes
\[
\left|\xi_c\right|<\frac{32}{3(\theta_0\kappa)^2}.
\]

Thus, for representative defect strengths:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=0.1
\Longrightarrow
|\xi_c/\xi_E|<1066.666\ldots
}
\label{eq:cont_window_01}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=0.3
\Longrightarrow
|\xi_c/\xi_E|<118.518\ldots
}
\label{eq:cont_window_03}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=1
\Longrightarrow
|\xi_c/\xi_E|<10.666\ldots
}
\label{eq:cont_window_1}
\end{equation}

Hence in the natural small-defect regime \((\theta_0\kappa)^2\ll1\),
the \(R_c\)-window is extremely broad.
So the low-core inequality is not fine-tuned unless \(\xi_c/\xi_E\) is abnormally large.

\section{6. Bulk mass parameter}

The bulk mass parameter is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\label{eq:cont_muinf}
\end{equation}
In the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\label{eq:cont_muinf_vac}
\end{equation}
If the standard radial convention fixes
\[
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:cont_muinf_sign}
\end{equation}

Thus the bulk-side sign audit is reduced to the sign of the asymptotic mass function \(m(\sigma_\infty)\).

\section{7. What remains genuinely unfixed}

The uploaded notes do \emph{not} yet supply numerical branch values for
\[
\xi_E,\qquad \xi_c,\qquad z_{0,0},\qquad m(\sigma_\infty),\qquad z_0(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
Therefore the present coefficient-finding status is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the branch-level formulas for \(a_0,b_0,c_0,R_c,\mu_\infty\) are explicit;
\item \(c_0=0\) is completely fixed for the present pure-\(E\) branch;
\item the sign conditions reduce to
\[
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\left|\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\]
plus the remote-gap inequality;
\item the remaining unknowns are finite branch data, not conceptual objects.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

For the explicit canonical branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
}
\]
the Bloch/Class-II coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
g_E
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\]

Hence the radial core coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
c_0=0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
\qquad
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\]

In the practical lowest-channel case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,\qquad \kappa_{\rm comp}\ge 1,
\]
the one-mode criterion reduces to
\[
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
}
\]
together with
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

For the unit benchmark
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=\xi_E=z_{0,0}=1,
\]
this becomes
\[
\boxed{
b_0\approx 0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
c_0=0,
\qquad
R_c=0.09375\,\xi_c\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\]

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=0.1 \Rightarrow |\xi_c|<1066.67,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=0.3 \Rightarrow |\xi_c|<118.52,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=1 \Rightarrow |\xi_c|<10.67.
}
\]

So the low-core inequality is naturally broad in the small-defect regime.
The remaining unfixed inputs are the finite branch data
\[
\boxed{
\xi_E,\qquad \xi_c,\qquad z_{0,0},\qquad \mu_\infty,\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Bulk-Mass Sign Audit for the Explicit Canonical Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

For the explicit branch
\[
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
\]
the transport-side coefficients are already fixed.
The remaining nontrivial post-acceptance radial condition is now the bulk-mass sign
\[
\mu_\infty>0.
\]

The exact constitutive formula is already known:
\[
\mu(r)
=
\frac{
m(\bar\sigma(r))
-
3\chi_X(r)u_X(\bar\sigma(r))
}{
z_0(\bar\sigma(r))
},
\]
so the asymptotic bulk parameter is
\[
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
\]

Thus the sign audit reduces to a finite constitutive inequality.

\section{1. Explicit branch input}

For the explicit canonical branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
}
\]
the already extracted transport coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:mu_gc}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:mu_gego}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=0,
\qquad
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
}
\label{eq:mu_a0b0c0}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{g_c}{g_E}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:mu_Rc}
\end{equation}

The practical one-mode criterion is therefore reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:mu_practical}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact asymptotic bulk mass formula}

The asymptotic effective mass is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\label{eq:mu_exact}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact sign condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
\Bigl[m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\Bigr]\,
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_sign_general}
\end{equation}

If the standard normalization convention fixes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0,
}
\label{eq:mu_z0_positive}
\end{equation}
then the condition simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_sign_simple}
\end{equation}

Thus the bulk-side sign audit is reduced to one scalar competition:
the positive asymptotic mass contribution \(m(\sigma_\infty)\) must dominate the asymptotic Class-II correction \(3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\).

\section{3. Simplest vacuum branch}

In the simplest vacuum branch one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_\infty=0.
}
\label{eq:mu_vacuum_chi0}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\label{eq:mu_vacuum}
\end{equation}

So, under the standard positive normalization \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_vacuum_sign}
\end{equation}

Therefore, in this simplest branch, the bulk-mass condition is not a dynamical balance anymore.
It is reduced to the sign of the asymptotic mass function \(m(\sigma_\infty)\).

\section{4. Non-vacuum asymptotic Class-II branch}

If \(\chi_\infty\neq0\), then the exact condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}
\qquad
\text{(assuming }z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\text{).}
\label{eq:mu_nonvac}
\end{equation}

This admits the following subcases.

\subsection*{Case A: \(u_X(\sigma_\infty)\ge 0\), \(\chi_\infty\ge 0\)}

Then the Class-II asymptotic correction reduces the bulk gap, and one needs the lower bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\ge 0.
}
\label{eq:mu_caseA}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Case B: \(u_X(\sigma_\infty)\le 0\), \(\chi_\infty\ge 0\)}

Then the Class-II correction helps the gap, and it is enough that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}
\label{eq:mu_caseB}
\end{equation}
which is weaker than simply demanding \(m(\sigma_\infty)>0\).

\subsection*{Case C: sign-indefinite asymptotic sector}

If the signs of \(\chi_\infty\) and \(u_X(\sigma_\infty)\) are not known, then
the exact sign audit is still finite but genuinely branch-specific:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{sgn}\mu_\infty
=
\operatorname{sgn}\Bigl(m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)\Bigr)
}
\qquad
\text{(assuming }z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\text{).}
\label{eq:mu_caseC}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Combined practical criterion for the explicit branch}

For the branch \(T_\star=T^1,\gamma_E=1,\gamma_O=0\), the practical lowest-channel acceptance problem becomes

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
}
\label{eq:mu_Rc_window}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0,
}
\label{eq:mu_alpha_positive}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0
\qquad
\text{(assuming }z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\text{),}
}
\label{eq:mu_bulk_positive}
\end{equation}
together with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:mu_remote_gap}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire post-acceptance one-mode verification of this explicit branch reduces to four finite scalar checks.

\section{6. Unit benchmark}

Take the unit benchmark
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=\xi_E=\xi_c=z_{0,0}=1.
\]
Then
\[
R_c=0.09375\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=0.1
\Longrightarrow
R_c=9.375\times 10^{-4},
}
\label{eq:mu_bench_01}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=0.3
\Longrightarrow
R_c=8.4375\times 10^{-3},
}
\label{eq:mu_bench_03}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa=1
\Longrightarrow
R_c=9.375\times 10^{-2}.
}
\label{eq:mu_bench_1}
\end{equation}

Hence the \(R_c\)-window is naturally satisfied in the small-defect regime.

If one additionally takes the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\), then the only remaining bulk sign check is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:mu_bench_final}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest status}

What is now explicit for the branch \(T_\star=T^1,\gamma_E=1,\gamma_O=0\):

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(g_c,g_E,g_O\);
\item \(a_0,b_0,c_0\) in terms of \(\xi_E,\xi_c,z_{0,0}\);
\item the exact ratio
\[
R_c=\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\frac{3}{32}\alpha_X(\theta_0\kappa)^2;
\]
\item the exact bulk-mass sign condition
\[
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0
\]
under \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\).
\end{enumerate}

What is still not numerically fixed by the uploaded notes is the actual branch data
\[
\xi_E,\qquad \xi_c,\qquad z_{0,0},\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
\chi_\infty,\qquad
u_X(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

So the remaining frontier is not structural.
It is the finite insertion of asymptotic constitutive data.

\section{Final Summary}

For the explicit canonical branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
}
\]
the post-acceptance one-defect/one-mode problem reduces to four scalar checks:

\[
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

The ratio parameter is already explicit:
\[
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\]

The bulk mass parameter is exactly
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\]

Hence, under the standard convention \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\),
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\]

In the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\), this simplifies to
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\]

For the unit benchmark
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=\xi_E=\xi_c=z_{0,0}=1,
\]
one gets
\[
\boxed{
R_c=0.09375\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
}
\]
so in the small-defect regime the \(R_c\)-window is automatically broad:
\[
\theta_0\kappa=0.1 \Rightarrow R_c=9.375\times10^{-4},
\]
\[
\theta_0\kappa=0.3 \Rightarrow R_c=8.4375\times10^{-3},
\]
\[
\theta_0\kappa=1 \Rightarrow R_c=9.375\times10^{-2}.
\]

Thus the genuinely nontrivial remaining branch inputs are
\[
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
\chi_\infty,\qquad
u_X(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

So the current explicit branch is already reduced to a finite asymptotic constitutive-data audit.

\section{Continuation of Coefficient-Finding for the Explicit Canonical Branch}

\section{Branch choice and canonical normalization}

We continue with the explicit branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=1,
\qquad
\gamma_O=0,
}
\]
and use the canonical one-mediator normalization
\[
\boxed{
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1.
}
\]

The one-mediator truncation gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2},
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}=0.
}
\label{eq:cont2_transport_point}
\end{equation}

Using
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:cont2_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:cont2_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the exact transport/Bloch dictionary
\[
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O,
\]
we simply have
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E=\alpha,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:cont2_gs}
\end{equation}

Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c
\approx
0.03188319195\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^3,
}
\label{eq:cont2_gc_num}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E
\approx
0.34008738079\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:cont2_ge_num}
\end{equation}

\section{Radial core coefficients}

Introduce the matching constants
\[
g_E^{\rm core}=\xi_E g_E,
\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}=\xi_c g_c,
\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}=\xi_O g_O,
\qquad
\xi_E,\xi_c,\xi_O>0.
\]
Then
\[
a_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}+g_c^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{g_O^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}}.
\]

Thus, for the present branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:cont2_b0}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_0=0,
}
\label{eq:cont2_c0}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa
+
\frac{\xi_c}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:cont2_a0}
\end{equation}

Factorizing \(b_0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
}
\label{eq:cont2_a0_factor}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{g_c}{g_E}
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:cont2_Rc}
\end{equation}

Therefore, assuming \(z_{0,0}>0\) and \(\xi_E>0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0.
}
\label{eq:cont2_b0_sign}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0>0
\iff
b_0>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
1+R_c>0.
}
\label{eq:cont2_a0_sign}
\end{equation}

\section{Bulk mass parameter}

The exact asymptotic bulk parameter is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\label{eq:cont2_muinf}
\end{equation}
Under the standard sign convention
\[
z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:cont2_muinf_sign}
\end{equation}
In the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:cont2_muinf_vac}
\end{equation}

\section{Carrier acceptance}

At carrier level the branch is accepted iff
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]
For the present branch this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0,
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:cont2_carrier_accept}
\end{equation}
Indeed,
\[
\lambda_\parallel\propto \alpha_X\beta_X(\theta_0\kappa)^3,
\qquad
\alpha\propto \beta_X(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
\beta=0.
\]

\section{Remote-gap support theorem inserted for this branch}

The fully inserted Step-IV gate is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:cont2_remote_gate}
\end{equation}

In canonical normalization \(C_E=C_O=1\), this simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\left[
2\kappa\rho
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:cont2_remote_gate_canonical}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:cont2_remote_gate_canonical} holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
>0,
}
\label{eq:cont2_remote_gap}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
}
\label{eq:cont2_Heff_gap}
\end{equation}

\section{Practical one-mode criterion for the explicit branch}

In the practically important case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,\qquad \kappa_{\rm comp}\ge1,
\]
the one-mode criterion reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:cont2_practical_final}
\end{equation}

Substituting the present branch data gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
}
\label{eq:cont2_ratio_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
}
\label{eq:cont2_alpha_positive}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0
\qquad
(\text{assuming }z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0),
}
\label{eq:cont2_mu_positive}
\end{equation}
and the remote-gap inequality \eqref{eq:cont2_remote_gate_canonical}.

\section{Unit benchmark}

Take
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=\xi_E=\xi_c=z_{0,0}=1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=1,\ \gamma_O=0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\approx 0.03188319195\,(\theta_0\kappa)^3,
\qquad
g_E\approx 0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
g_O=0,
}
\label{eq:cont2_unit_gs}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0\approx 0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
c_0=0,
}
\label{eq:cont2_unit_b0}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_c=0.09375\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
}
\label{eq:cont2_unit_Rc}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0
\approx
0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa)\,
\bigl[1+0.09375(\theta_0\kappa)^2\bigr].
}
\label{eq:cont2_unit_a0}
\end{equation}

Representative values:
\[
\theta_0\kappa=0.1
\Rightarrow
R_c=9.375\times10^{-4},
\]
\[
\theta_0\kappa=0.3
\Rightarrow
R_c=8.4375\times10^{-3},
\]
\[
\theta_0\kappa=1
\Rightarrow
R_c=9.375\times10^{-2}.
\]

Hence the \(R_c\)-window is automatically broad in the natural small-defect regime.

\section{Honest endpoint}

For the explicit canonical branch \(T_\star=T^1,\gamma_E=1,\gamma_O=0\), the following are now explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item transport-side coefficients \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\);
\item radial core coefficients \((a_0,b_0,c_0)\) up to finite matching constants;
\item exact ratio \(R_c\);
\item exact sign reduction of \(\mu_\infty\);
\item the branch-inserted remote-gap gate.
\end{enumerate}

What is still not numerically fixed in the uploaded notes is the finite branch data
\[
\xi_E,\qquad \xi_c,\qquad z_{0,0},\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty),\qquad z_0(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
\chi_\infty,\qquad u_X(\sigma_\infty),
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{high,non}},\qquad
K_a,\qquad
\widetilde K_a,\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]
Therefore the remaining frontier is not structural.
It is the final finite constitutive-data insertion.

\section{Final Summary}

For the explicit canonical branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
}
\]
the one-mediator transport-side coefficients in canonical normalization are
\[
\boxed{
g_c
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
g_E
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\]

Hence the radial core coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}g_E,
\qquad
c_0=0,
\qquad
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\]

The bulk mass condition is exactly
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
},
}
\]
so under \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\),
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\]

The branch-inserted Step-IV remote-gap gate is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\left[
2\kappa\rho
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

Therefore the practical one-mode criterion for this branch reduces to the four scalar checks
\[
\boxed{
\left|
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}
\right|
<
\frac{32}{3|\alpha_X|(\theta_0\kappa)^2},
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

For the unit benchmark
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=\xi_E=\xi_c=z_{0,0}=1,
\]
one gets
\[
\boxed{
b_0\approx 0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
c_0=0,
\qquad
R_c=0.09375\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
a_0
\approx
0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa)\,
\bigl[1+0.09375(\theta_0\kappa)^2\bigr].
}
\]

Thus the \(R_c\)-window is naturally broad in the small-defect regime, and the genuinely nontrivial remaining branch data are
\[
\boxed{
\xi_E,\ \xi_c,\ z_{0,0},\ 
m(\sigma_\infty),\ z_0(\sigma_\infty),\ \chi_\infty,\ u_X(\sigma_\infty),\
C_{\mathrm{high,non}},\ K_a,\ \widetilde K_a,\ \eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

\section{Continuation of Coefficient-Finding: Explicit Remote-Gap Insertion for the Canonical Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

For the explicit branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
}
\]
the transport-side coefficients and the radial dictionary are already explicit.
The remaining coefficient-finding task is to insert this branch into the final Step-IV remote-gap inequality and isolate the genuinely branch-dependent finite data.

\section{1. Fixed transport-side coefficients}

Under the canonical one-mediator normalization
\[
\boxed{
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
}
\]
the explicit branch coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c
=
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:rem_gc}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E
=
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
g_O=\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:rem_gego}
\end{equation}

Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c
\approx
0.03188319195\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^3,
}
\label{eq:rem_gc_num}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E
\approx
0.34008738079\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
g_O=0.
}
\label{eq:rem_ge_num}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Fixed radial coefficients}

Using
\[
g_E^{\rm core}=\xi_E g_E,
\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}=\xi_c g_c,
\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}=\xi_O g_O,
\]
the radial coefficients become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,g_E
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\,
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:rem_b0}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_0=0,
}
\label{eq:rem_c0}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
\qquad
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c}{\xi_E}\,
\frac{3}{32}\,
\alpha_X\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:rem_a0_Rc}
\end{equation}

Thus the practical radial sign conditions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0>0
\iff
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\theta_0\kappa>0,
}
\label{eq:rem_b0_sign}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0>0
\iff
b_0>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
1+R_c>0.
}
\label{eq:rem_a0_sign}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Bulk mass parameter}

The exact asymptotic bulk parameter remains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\label{eq:rem_muinf}
\end{equation}
Under the standard convention \(z_0(\sigma_\infty)>0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:rem_muinf_sign}
\end{equation}
In the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0
\iff
m(\sigma_\infty)>0.
}
\label{eq:rem_muinf_vac}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact benchmark side}

The final benchmark side is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\label{eq:rem_bench}
\end{equation}

Thus the only genuinely model-specific benchmark piece is the same-shell non-enriched entry
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\]
which is already reduced to one finite Hermitian eigenvalue computation.

\section{5. Branch-inserted residual side}

The exact final inserted residual side is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:rem_residual_full}
\end{equation}

In the canonical normalization \(C_E=C_O=1\), this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
4\kappa\rho
+
\frac{2}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:rem_residual_canonical}
\end{equation}

This is the fully branch-inserted Step-IV residual budget.

\section{6. Exact branch-inserted remote-gap gate}

Therefore, for the explicit branch \(T_\star=T^1,\gamma_E=1,\gamma_O=0\), the exact Step-IV gate is the single inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
4\kappa\rho
+
\frac{2}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2
\right)
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:rem_gate_branch}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:rem_gate_branch} holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:rem_gap_branch}
\end{equation}

Thus the remote sector is spectrally isolated.

\section{7. Full practical criterion for this branch}

The practical lowest-channel criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\theta_0\kappa>0,
\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)>0,
\qquad
\eqref{eq:rem_gate_branch}\ \text{holds}.
}
\label{eq:rem_full_practical_branch}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the full coefficient-finding program for this explicit branch is reduced to the finite data
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\xi_E,\qquad
\xi_c,\qquad
z_{0,0},\qquad
m(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
z_0(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
\chi_\infty,\qquad
u_X(\sigma_\infty),\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},\qquad
C_{\mathrm{high,non}},\qquad
K_a,\qquad
\widetilde K_a,\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:rem_remaining_data}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Unit benchmark}

Take
\[
\alpha_X=\beta_X=M_X=\xi_E=\xi_c=z_{0,0}=1.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_0\approx 0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
c_0=0,
\qquad
R_c=0.09375\,(\theta_0\kappa)^2,
}
\label{eq:rem_unit1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_0
\approx
0.34008738079\,(\theta_0\kappa)\,
\bigl[1+0.09375(\theta_0\kappa)^2\bigr].
}
\label{eq:rem_unit2}
\end{equation}

For representative defect strengths:
\[
\theta_0\kappa=0.1
\Rightarrow
R_c=9.375\times 10^{-4},
\]
\[
\theta_0\kappa=0.3
\Rightarrow
R_c=8.4375\times 10^{-3},
\]
\[
\theta_0\kappa=1
\Rightarrow
R_c=9.375\times 10^{-2}.
\]

Hence the \(R_c\)-window is automatically broad in the natural small-defect regime, and the genuinely nontrivial remaining checks are the bulk sign and the remote-gap inequality.

\section{Final Summary}

For the explicit canonical branch
\[
\boxed{

the coefficient-finding program can now be written entirely in finite algebraic form.

The transport-side coefficients are

\quad

The exact branch-inserted remote-gap gate is

+

Thus the full practical lowest-channel condition for this branch is reduced to four finite checks:

\boxed{

\qquad

Under the unit benchmark
